Yoshida Cabinet's Position Becomes More Stable 57

Liberal and Progressive Parties to Merge

[Our Tokyo Correspondent, 16th] When the Yoshida Cabinet was formed, the people recognized it as a constitutional cabinet, that is, the purpose of the Yoshida Cabinet was to amend the constitution and submit it for passage at this session of the Provisional Diet. After the Diet session ended, it would collapse. However, the session of this Diet has been specially extended, and there is talk of further extensions, and Yoshida himself seems confident that he can maintain his cabinet until the Japanese peace conference. Generally speaking, such confidence on Yoshida's part is not impossible to realize. Because foreign trade is about to open up, the food shortage has gradually eased, and the Socialist Party's offensive against the government is not as fierce as imagined. In the negotiations of this National Railway labor strike, the Socialist Party's attitude was quite moderate and did not take unified action with the Communist Party. In the statement, it only hoped for a satisfactory solution, fearing that this strike would develop into a general political strike. The Communist Party originally wanted to transform this National Railway labor strike into a nationwide political strike, and then overthrow the Yoshida Cabinet, but this plan ultimately failed. The National Railway labor strike suddenly reached a compromise one night and canceled the decision to strike, which of course cannot be attributed entirely without the support of foreign aid forces. The resolution of the National Railway labor strike can be said to be a tonic for the Yoshida Cabinet, which is why the Liberal Party supported Yoshida as president. The Liberal and Progressive parties acknowledge that Yoshida will remain Prime Minister when the Japanese peace conference is held, and Progressive Party President Hiranuma will serve as the plenipotentiary representative to the peace conference. Therefore, the merger of the Liberal and Progressive parties can be achieved. Recently, rumors of a merger between the Liberal and Progressive parties have been growing, and it is recognized that it is possible to achieve this by next spring. Currently, the Liberal and Progressive parties have a total of 250 seats in the Diet, just over half, but Yoshida is still worried about his weakness and is trying to win over minority parties. Yoshida's recent reception of the Shinseikai also shows Yoshida's attempt to win over various parties.

Youth Corps Second National Congress Declaration: Text Continued from Page Two 60

We believe that the biggest obstacle to national construction at present is the inertia of the general public after the war, and also due to the sabotage and obstruction of the Communist Party. We want to revive the economy and build society, while the Communist Party destroys transportation and breaches dikes. We want to prosper the countryside and restore industry; while the Communist Party wants to destroy the countryside and destroy industry. We want to coordinate agricultural and industrial production to improve people's lives; while the Communist Party separates agriculture from industry and isolates cities from villages. As for the overall construction: if transportation cannot be restored, materials cannot circulate, the economy is divided, and society is in chaos, of course, endless difficulties will be added; but the pain of our people's livelihood cannot be relieved without intensifying national construction, and the survival and development of the country cannot be guaranteed without intensifying national construction. Therefore, our national youth must recognize their goals, take responsibility, endure hardship, eliminate the inertia of complacency and fear of difficulty, work together, break through any obstacles and difficulties, and intensify our work of national construction to comfort the spirits of the martyrs of the Anti-Japanese War. Regarding the implementation of the Three Principles of the People, it is the unshirkable responsibility of the government. We believe that the implementation of nationalism has already achieved considerable success, and what urgently needs to be done now is the thorough implementation of democracy and people's livelihood. Regarding democracy, we believe that it is necessary to establish the rule of law, guarantee freedom, rectify political morality, eliminate corruption, improve administrative efficiency, effectively implement local self-government, establish people's representative organs at all levels, improve grassroots political organizations, and support the real power of the people, so that democratic constitutionalism has a solid foundation. Regarding people's livelihood, we believe that the government should be determined to earnestly implement the policy of equalizing land ownership and controlling capital. Regarding the former, it is necessary to effectively implement the 25% rent reduction, implement land laws and regulations, equalize land distribution, ensure that tillers have their land, and advocate the establishment of cooperative farms and collective farms to increase agricultural production and improve farmers' lives. Regarding the latter, it is necessary to strengthen financial management, suppress high-interest exploitation, guide commercial capital towards industrial production, promote labor-management coordination, protect the interests of workers, support agricultural and industrial organizations, establish a social insurance system, and effectively promote cooperative undertakings such as production, transportation, and consumption. Only in this way can our work of revolutionary national construction not be empty talk, and can we gain the trust of compatriots throughout the country. (We are confident that we are enthusiastic, brave, and pure Chinese revolutionary youth.) We have revolutionary beliefs and are by no means pessimistic about the future of China and the world. We believe that the Three Principles of the People is a doctrine that follows the principles of heaven, responds to human feelings, conforms to the trend of the world, and meets the needs of the people. As long as we work hard to implement it, there is no reason why it will not succeed. We all have a service-oriented, creative, correct, and noble outlook on life. We care about Chinese politics and the future of the country and nation, and are willing to sacrifice, struggle, and contribute everything to complete the great cause of revolutionary national construction. We are willing to maintain the loyalty and purity of youth for a long time and eliminate the secular idea of ​​getting promoted and making a fortune. We Youth Corps members pledge to abide by the Corps charter, serve the people, and sacrifice for the revolution. We are willing to be an unsung hero of revolutionary national construction. We absolutely abide by national laws and regulations and strictly abide by the disciplines of our country. We pledge to be believers in the Three Principles of the People and, under the leadership of our Corps Leader, do our best to build the country, and strive to be fighters for the national revolution. What we urgently request from the government today is to give the young men and women of our country ample opportunities for further education and employment, to give them ample opportunities to participate in grassroots national construction work, to cultivate the spirit of independent creation of young men and women, to strengthen all kinds of science and education related to national construction in national schools, and to be responsible for educating and supporting young compatriots in the border areas and overseas, so that all young people in the country learn modern knowledge and skills and concentrate under the banner of the Three Principles of the People to create a new China owned by the people, governed by the people, and enjoyed by the people.

(4) Our Corps has been established for eight years. Our Corps members have been constantly admonishing and earnestly expecting us to be revolutionary cadres and to make us the driving force of national construction. However, reviewing the past, the organization is not strict enough, and the work is not solid enough. For any aspect of the Corps, we need to make further efforts. We deeply miss every comrade who struggled and sacrificed his life against the enemy puppets during the Anti-Japanese War. In order to carry forward their glorious history, we should be more vigorous, self-improving, and unremitting to improve our Youth Corps.

We feel that in order to adapt to the needs of the times and strengthen the revolutionary forces, to eliminate the obstacles to revolutionary national construction, and to achieve the task of revolutionary national construction, our Corps must enrich the interior and strengthen the organization, such as the establishment of the democratic centralism system, grassroots organizational cadres, the implementation of policies, the recruitment of outstanding talents, etc., all of which are related to the future success or failure of the Corps. Detailed methods have now been determined and must be strictly implemented. This conference of ours has even more important decisions for the entire party: (1) Clearly stipulate the direction of the Corps' work in the future, so that the efforts of our Corps members in the future can be more practical and progressive; (2) Under the same doctrine and the same leader, the Party and the Corps share the common task of national revolution, but the cadres of the Party and the Corps are clearly divided, so that each specializes in its duties and does its best, so that the cadres have specific responsibilities and the work has specialized contributions, so that our Corps becomes a sound and strong revolutionary group of Three Principles of the People youth, and fulfills its important responsibilities to the times.

Finally, we would like to emphasize a few points: (1) The direction of the Corps members' efforts in the future is to tend towards active construction, and to shift from empty political activities to grassroots social service work. We must recognize that the root cause of our cultural and economic backwardness is the poison of the thousands of years of the wrong idea of ​​the literati and officials who get something for nothing, which leads to the separation of knowledge and production, and the separation of knowledge and occupation. In the future, we must be determined to establish professional positions, enter farms, factories, mines, enter the border areas, and participate in actual production work, in order to correct the general atmosphere of idleness and lay the foundation for national construction. (2) We are all Chinese youth. We must be independent and self-reliant in spirit and never lose self-confidence. We must not unknowingly become slaves to others. Of course, we must learn from others as much as possible in science and technology; but we must especially remember that we learn from others to enrich ourselves, not to lose ourselves. (3) We respect academic freedom and freedom of thought. Regarding the study of communism and the belief in communism, we stand on the position of academic freedom of thought and do not oppose it; however, the Communist Party's behavior of undermining national unity, disrupting social order, and destroying national morality not only destroys the future of our country, but also harms our youth as slaves. We truly patriotic youth must never tolerate it. (4) We firmly believe that we can only do something after we have not done something. We do not become officials, we despise politicians, we must work hard in various construction works, and are willing to contribute our mind and energy to social services and to production undertakings. We believe that transforming society is the fundamental way to transform politics, and building society is the fundamental way to build the country. If the country abandons various undertakings in society and does not harmonize, then clarifying politics and building the country will never have hope. (5) We must develop the ability to make correct judgments, distinguish right from wrong, and distinguish good from bad. We must oppose any dark forces that use our youth, deceive our youth, lure our youth, and make our youth embark on harming the country, harming the nation, and disrupting social morality, and we must thoroughly eliminate them. Every one of us youth has an independent and autonomous personality and has a sacred obligation to the country and nation. We must never allow others to use us to harm our country, harm our nation, disrupt our unity, disrupt our revolution, and thus ruin the future of our youth. I want to awaken the youth of the whole country, raise vigilance, and be wary of people who come to use our youth and harm our youth. (6) We must follow the Corps Leader's instructions in "China's Destiny" and the decisions of the First National Congress, earnestly call on the youth of the whole country to participate in the five major constructions, and the Corps members should take the lead in advocating and serving as a demonstration. We must pay more attention to scientific research, and it is necessary to implement social services, and cultivate our youth and train our youth from practical work. Otherwise, they will not be youth of the Three Principles of the People. Our Youth Corps must not tolerate such backward youth and recognize them as Corps members and comrades.

What we have said above is our common understanding, which is the call we have made on behalf of the youth of the country. Extraordinary times require extraordinary undertakings and extraordinary efforts. Our generation must not relax our mission to the times. Everything can be given to others, only the obligations and responsibilities to the country and the nation cannot be given to others. Everything can be compromised, only those who harm the interests of the country and the nation cannot be compromised. Comrades! Compatriots! The wind and rain are dark, but the rooster crows incessantly. We must unite as one, overcome difficulties, destroy the obstacles to the revolution, and save our country. We must take responsibility, hold high the torch of the Three Principles of the People, and strive forward, so that the new China of the Three Principles of the People and the new world of universal love and great harmony will be realized before us as soon as possible. (End)

City Council Commemorative Week: Speaker Pan's Earnest Words, Hoping Councilors Demonstrate True Democratic Spirit and Conduct Reasonable Scrutiny of the Municipal Government Budget 61

[Our Newspaper] Speaker Pan stated in his address during the Commemorative Week: "Since the City Council began, it feels as if we have already walked halfway. The past week's agenda has been filled with reports and inquiries. In addition, we have held two subcommittee reviews and one full council review, but we have not yet reached the stage of discussion and resolution. Whether the mission can be completed still depends on our efforts this week. Currently, the outside world is very concerned about this council because its mission is extremely important. How the spirit of democracy is manifested in Shanghai, and thus in China, depends entirely on this council. The Shanghai Evening Post has criticized, saying: If you want to know the spirit of popular opinion bodies under the Kuomintang government, you only need to look at the current Shanghai City Council. Therefore, today, with the utmost sincerity, I hope that everyone will demonstrate the best performance and achievements in implementing a democratic political system. We must use a truth-seeking attitude to distinguish right from wrong, so that people understand that we are indeed sincere and genuine representatives of the people. Secondly, some people often think that the council and the government are in opposing positions, but this view is not a true understanding of democracy. For example, the British government itself is formed by the parliament, so of course there is no mutual opposition. Although China is still in a transitional period, and the municipal government has not yet reached the stage of being democratically elected, if we regard the entire Shanghai as a large company, the citizens are the shareholders, the municipal government is the management, and the council is like the board of directors, it is definitely not a mutually hostile relationship. The Shanghai Evening Post also said: Whether Shanghai continues to develop into a world-renowned metropolis or regresses into a second-rate, unimportant city in the future, the responsibility lies entirely with this council. Therefore, we must especially value our role as an institution that provides direction and decides policies. I hope to encourage everyone to work together to complete this important task. I hope that the budget review can be completed no later than the fourth subcommittee meeting. Regarding the municipal government's work plan, my personal thought is that the work plan is actually an explanation of the budget. It is really ridiculous that everyone is now separating them. Fortunately, almost three months have passed in the second half of the year. If this review cannot achieve the ideal result, we must proceed cautiously in the next year. If we want the municipal government to do things, we must give it money. Without money, how can things be done? Although we should, of course, still save where we can. Reviewing the budget and final accounts is really the focus of this council's mission. If we can perform well in this regard, we will lay the cornerstone of democratic politics. Therefore, we should conduct a reasonable review of this budget. As long as the municipal government is truly doing things, we should give it money, whether it is through increased taxes or issuing public bonds. This is my personal opinion."

Armed Agencies Cannot Be Driven Away; They Erect Machine Guns to Resist: Dai Jimin Reports on the Numerous Difficulties in Housing Allocation 62

After a ten-minute break following Commemorative Week, Dai Jimin, Secretary-General of the Housing Allocation Committee, reported on the committee's work as follows:

The Housing Allocation Committee was only established on April 20 of this year. Previously, there were approximately 8,000 Japanese-owned houses in the Hongkou district. After the Japanese residents were successively repatriated in February and March, the remaining houses were occupied by powerful individuals. The Japanese Property Management Office, together with the municipal government and relevant agencies, organized a cleanup team to investigate. The results were found to be very bad. The Executive Yuan believed that it was necessary to establish a specialized agency to handle the matter, so preparations began on April 18, and the Housing Allocation Committee was established on April 20. The mayor serves concurrently as the chairman, and the committee is divided into general affairs, investigation, execution, and allocation groups. Existing personnel from relevant agencies were transferred to perform the work.

After its establishment, the initial plan was to first clarify the supply and demand situation, such as the number of houses available for allocation and the number needed by various agencies, and then allocate them fairly. However, in fact, the investigation work took a lot of time, and it was not completed by the end of July, so the method was changed: investigation and allocation were carried out simultaneously.

The allocation standard is based on the order in which applications are submitted, which are then submitted to the general assembly for review and approval. In fact, there are fewer than 200 truly vacant houses; the rest have already been occupied. For those agencies or private individuals who have moved in without authorization, the Allocation Committee allows them to fill out reports for review. Those who meet the regulations are issued permits, and those who do not meet the regulations are attempted to be evicted. However, eviction is very difficult. Some armed agencies simply cannot be driven away and even erect machine guns to resist. Later, they had no choice but to negotiate with their supervising agencies. In addition, for houses that originally had owners, the China Trust Bureau (中信局) uniformly leases them, so that the owners receive reasonable rent.

Of the more than 8,000 houses, some are municipal properties and are not included in the allocation. Only over 5,000 houses are available for allocation, while the number of applications from various parties requires more than 10,000 houses. Currently, permits have been issued for 2,439 houses, allocated to the Army 987 houses, the Air Force 136 houses, the Navy 79 houses, and others 1,237 houses. Among them, 1,524 houses were occupied first and then issued permits.

Municipal Government's Budget Expenditures for the Second Half of the Year 63

[Our Newspaper] The municipal government's budget expenditures for the second half of the 35th year (1946): The administrative part accounts for 14.4% of the total budget expenditures, totaling 13.2 billion. The operational part accounts for 85.6% of the total budget, totaling 71 billion.

The regular expenses of the administrative part, including salaries and office expenses for the municipal government and various bureaus, total 1.2 billion, plus living allowances, totaling 9.5 billion. As for the regular expenses of the operational part, they are the salaries of personnel handling various businesses, such as teachers and staff in various schools, workers in various district public works offices and factories, various health centers, various relief homes, and various police substations, totaling 4.7 billion, plus living allowances of 36.3 billion, totaling 41 billion.

The temporary expenses of the administrative part are the purchase and repair expenses of the municipal government and various bureaus, such as printing, furniture, gasoline consumption, house and vehicle repairs, advertising, training, etc., totaling 3.7 billion. The temporary expenses of the operational part are the materials and tools needed to conduct various businesses, such as adding class equipment to municipal schools and subsidizing private schools, maintaining roads, building new roads, adding street lights, opening civilian hospitals, running cleaning stations, subsidizing free hospital beds in municipal hospitals, police winter uniforms, printing costs, etc., totaling 30 billion.

Housing Allocation Subject to Criticism; Illegal Seizures Should Be Sanctioned; Demanding the Executive Yuan to Come Up With a Solution; Councilors' Interrogations Stirred Up Emotions 65

Councilors' interrogations regarding the Housing Allocation Committee were very heated. Eleven speakers, including Lu Huimin, Qu Yue, and Lu Yinchu, raised several points in their inquiries:

(1) The report's content is too vague, and the figures are not detailed enough. What is the total number of houses seized from the enemy that the Housing Allocation Committee received, and where are they located? A detailed disclosure is required.

(2) There are many unfair situations in the already allocated houses. Some individuals have been allocated two or three houses and are selling them for gold bars, while many public education agencies cannot be allocated any houses at all. What are the standards that the Allocation Committee is using? The names of the agencies and individuals that have been allocated houses must be made public.

(3) Illegal seizures are not only a disregard for the law, but also a national disgrace. This phenomenon must be corrected. The Allocation Committee should publish the names of those seizing agencies in detail in the newspaper and use the power of public opinion to sanction them.

(4) The government must issue a law that must be enforced. The Housing Allocation Measures are stipulated by the Executive Yuan. The Executive Yuan is the highest executive agency. If the laws and regulations it sets cannot be enforced, who else can enforce them? In fact, the original measures do have inappropriate aspects and should be revised or new measures should be formulated.

Chen Peide specifically raised the issue of Xie Jinyuan's widow's residence. He said that the government had long issued a clear order that the families of martyrs should have houses to live in. Why hasn't she been allocated one yet?

Zhang Zhihan believes that relying solely on the power of public opinion is not enough to stop the trend of seizures. He advocates that the council organize an agency with the support of all citizens to strengthen the work of housing allocation.

Wang Jian'e raised specific facts, saying that the district office needs a place to work, and there are three houses in the district: one is occupied by Zha Liangjian, one is used by the Security Department's Detective Team, and one is used by the Military Police. When he asked the Allocation Committee, the reply was that they were already occupied, so don't think about them anymore. He wants to ask: What exactly does "allocation" mean?

Continuing Budget Review: The Ninth Group Held Its Fourth Meeting Yesterday; Heads of Various Bureaus Attended and Reported Separately 66

The City Council held review meetings simultaneously in ten groups yesterday afternoon at 3:00 PM. The ninth group was the most important because it continued to review the municipal government's new budget for the second half of the year. The ninth group held its fourth meeting yesterday, and various bureaus continued to report on their financial revenues and expenditures and budgets. In addition to oral reports, written materials were submitted to the council for reference. Attendees included the municipal government's accountant, heads of various bureaus, and accounting directors, totaling more than ten people. The meeting was presided over by Xu Yongzuo, the convener of the group. Councilors raised questions about any unclear or insufficiently detailed points in the reports of various bureaus, and the responsible bureaus supplemented their explanations.

Public Utilities

First, Zhao Huijue, Director of the Public Utilities Bureau, reported on the bureau's total budget for the second half of the year, totaling 4.3 billion yuan, of which regular administrative management expenses accounted for 16% of the total budget, operating expenses accounted for 62%, and subsidies for operating expenses accounted for 11%. Then, the affiliated agencies reported on the operating revenue and expenditure budget for the second half of the year for the Public Bus Preparatory Office. The revenue was 3.6 billion yuan, equal to the expenditure. Expansion expenses were 2.2 billion yuan, part of which was a loan and part of which was subsidized by the municipal government. The Pudong Water Company's operating revenue was 5.85 million yuan, the water supply station 3.93 million yuan, and the ship water supply 3.28 million yuan. On the expenditure side: personnel and vehicle expenses were approximately 8 million yuan, start-up costs were 2 million yuan, chemical testing fees were 2 million yuan, and miscellaneous expenses were 2 million yuan. The Municipal Ferry Management Office's operating revenue was 1 billion yuan, offsetting the expenses, and the expenditure on improved assets after increased construction was 300 million yuan. The Wusong Coal Gas Plant's operating revenue was 740 million yuan, offsetting the expenses, and the expansion expenses were 1.3 billion yuan, which is expected to be completed within one year.

Police

Next, Yu Shuping, Deputy Director of the Police Bureau, reported. Yu said that the police bureau's budget was compiled based on the bureau's regular operations, as the bureau's work should be to consolidate public security, prohibit opium, manage traffic, rectify customs, organize the city appearance, and strengthen fire protection. The staffing was determined based on the importance of various tasks. According to the staffing, the total number of people was 20,000, and the current number was 13,000, a ratio of 1 to 300 to the citizens. Yu then analyzed the various fee categories and needs of the new budget and cited examples comparing them with the police expenses of the former concessions. "In the past, police expenses in the concessions accounted for 50% of the annual expenditure, and fire protection fees were an additional 4%, for a total of 54%, while according to the current new budget, it only accounts for 22% of the annual expenditure," he said.

Social Affairs

Li Jianhua, Deputy Director of the Social Affairs Bureau, reported that the bureau's budget for the second half of the year should be its minimum limit, such as the winter relief fund of only 35 million yuan, and the three public memorial ceremonies of only 3 million yuan. Other items include 30 million yuan for purchasing, repairing, and printing expenses, 14 million yuan for business and guidance operating expenses, 900,000 yuan for agricultural and forestry expansion guidance expenses, 1 million yuan for company and factory investigation guidance expenses, 1 million yuan for other investigation guidance expenses, 5 million yuan for small loan loss expenses, and 15 million yuan for relief business subsidy expenses.

Health

Zhang Wei, Director of the Health Bureau, reported that the funding for the second half of the year only increased by one time compared to the first half of the year. The plan is to achieve 70% technology and 30% administration. The total budget for the Health Bureau in the second half of the year is 13.6 billion yuan, of which administrative expenses account for 3.4%, and business management expenses account for 95.6%, including medical and equipment expenses accounting for 34.9%, environmental health accounting for 46.8%, health care expenses accounting for 12.7%, and epidemic prevention expenses accounting for 5.6%.

Education

Li Ximou, Deputy Director of the Education Bureau, reported that the total budget for the second half of the year is 16.2 billion yuan, 1.3 billion yuan for adding classes and starting expenses, more than 550 million yuan for supplementary equipment for municipal schools and institutions, 300 million yuan for board expenses for normal school students, 1 billion yuan for subsidies to private schools and institutions, and only 25 million yuan for administrative affairs. At the same time, the Civil Affairs Office also submitted a written report.

After the reports were completed, the councilors briefly expressed their opinions and adjourned the meeting, and decided to hold another closed-door review meeting tonight, and the heads of various bureaus were still invited to attend.

Regarding Public Utilities and Public Works 67

The fifth review committee had about 80 proposals related to public utilities and public works, so at the third review meeting yesterday, it was passed to merge all the proposals into 20 major cases. Two cases were discussed yesterday:

Unify Transportation Routes, Improve Traffic

(1) Regarding unifying tram and bus routes, increasing vehicles, improving traffic, and training staff, it is proposed that the Public Utilities Bureau be instructed to urge the relevant companies to implement it conscientiously. It was discussed by merging eight cases. After the review, four points were initially resolved: (1) Public utilities should be operated by private companies in principle. (2) The China Merchant Electricity Company should be quickly restored and protected. (3) Public buses should also be handled according to the first principle. (4) The methods discussed in the relevant proposals should be compiled by the secretary and sent to the Public Utilities Bureau for reference.

Restricting Electricity Use, Discontinuing Electric Heating

(2) Regarding the proposal to request the municipal government to restrict electricity consumption, it was reviewed by merging seven cases. As a result, the following was initially resolved: (1) To restrict electricity consumption for heating, it is proposed that the power company not be allowed to provide electric heating again this winter. The French Power Company will resume connecting electricity next month, which should be canceled. According to Zhao Zengjue, Director of the Public Utilities Bureau, if electric heating is stopped, 20,000 kilowatts can be saved, so the city's electricity will no longer need to be worried about. (2) Restricting electricity use should be based on the electricity consumption record of February of this year. For newly installed electricity users, it should be based on the electricity consumption record of August. Those who violate the regulations three times should be severely punished. Detailed measures will be formulated by the Public Utilities Bureau. (3) Military electricity should be charged to show restriction. It is proposed that the municipal government submit a request to the Ministry of National Defense to issue an order to the military to pay for the lamp oil fees for electricity use.

Soldiers Who Seize Houses Will Be Severely Punished According to Military Law; They Must All Evacuate Before the End of the Month 68

When the Songhu Garrison Headquarters held a week of fasting yesterday morning, Commander Xuan made an important report on the matter of soldiers seizing houses, stating that he had just received a telegram from Chairman Chiang, ordering that soldiers who illegally seize houses must immediately evacuate voluntarily. If it is verified, they will be severely punished according to military law. Xuan also stated that those who seize houses must evacuate before the end of the month, and those who fail to do so will be dealt with according to military law. Xuan will also convene a meeting of army, navy, and air force generals in the coming days.

Organizing an Observation Group to Investigate Foreign Education; Li Ximou Submitted a Proposal to Use the Education Bureau's Stipulated Subsidy for Private Schools to Supplement Free Quotas 69

The sixth review committee reviewed proposals related to education and culture, with Zhou Feicheng as chairman. First, similar proposals were merged and divided into more than twenty categories, such as increasing municipal primary schools, subsidizing private primary and secondary schools, increasing public schools, vocational schools, normal schools, and increasing teacher salaries.

Regarding the education budget, the municipal government stipulates that it accounts for 19.7% of the total budget. All members of this group believe that it should be increased, otherwise, educational construction cannot be started. Increasing it to 30% is the most ideal, and it should at least account for 25%.

There were 19 proposals related to increasing municipal primary schools, and two review committee members were assigned to sort them out. Due to time constraints, they were not reviewed.

Yesterday's main review work was related to the issue of tuition fees for private schools. Recently, councilors have strongly criticized the unrestricted tuition fees of private schools, so the committee members were very cautious when reviewing this case. Finally, the following review opinion was passed: "The tuition fees for private primary and secondary schools should be requested by the municipal government to be stipulated according to the price situation at that time, and detailed standards for use and distribution should be established and strictly supervised. Those who deliberately violate them should be punished."

Several private school principals who attended this group's review gave explanations on the tuition fees of private schools. They all believe that if they want to strengthen the teaching staff and develop education, the current tuition fees cannot be said to be too high. Li Ximou, Deputy Director of the Education Bureau, was also present and proposed that in addition to strictly stipulating a 20% free quota, the private school subsidy stipulated by the Education Bureau should be used to supplement the number of free places. The committee members also decided to report the situation of tuition fees in private schools at the general meeting and detail the difficulties.

As for the teacher respect fee, it has been decided to propose that it should not be collected at all levels of primary and secondary schools starting from the next semester. Regarding the case where teachers in various schools who have worked for ten years should be given one year of rest, with salaries and benefits paid as usual, it is proposed that the municipal government should implement it conscientiously.

The Education Bureau submitted a proposal to send an education observation group to investigate education abroad to serve as a reference for the restoration of the city's education. After review, the following method was decided: The Education Bureau should hire those who have contributed to the city's education and culture and those who have served in the city's education sector for more than ten years and have achieved outstanding results to form a foreign observation group.

Finally, it was decided to make a resolution on the Education Bureau's work report, and Huang Shijin, Chen Baotai, and Wang Liben were responsible for drafting it.

Reviewing Finance and Land Administration: Preliminary Resolutions on Important Cases 70

The third group reviewed finance and land administration proposals and held its third meeting yesterday. Excerpts of the preliminary resolutions are recorded as follows: (1) The case of not increasing rents was sent to the municipal government for consideration. (2) The practice of cracking down on second landlords' extra demands and malpractices should be strictly prohibited by the municipal government, and the municipal government should formulate measures for conscientious implementation. (3) The construction of affordable housing was sent to the municipal government for consideration. (4) The housing lease dispute case will be jointly discussed with the tenth group's Legislative Committee. (5) The case of investigating and clarifying wasteland and public property in the urban area for utilization was not passed and should be resubmitted with a real estate management method for approval. (6) The original tenant of a house has the right of first refusal to lease, but the landlord may refuse to renew the lease if there is a violation of the regulations (the method will be announced after being passed by the general meeting). (7) Stopping the collection of defense corps uniform fees and exempting the book industry from business tax have been sent to the municipal government to be handled by the Finance Bureau. (8) Returning civilian land occupied by the enemy and puppets should be handled quickly and conscientiously by the municipal government. (9) Dividing shared land to avoid disputes should be handled by the Land Administration Bureau.

The Housing Lease Management Committee Has Numerous Malpractices in Arbitration; The Tenth Group's Review of Regulations Sparked FierCE Debate; Three Principles Were Decided: Arbitration Should Adopt a Collegial System 71

The tenth review committee was responsible for reviewing legislative proposals. The Housing Lease Management Committee regulations were discussed yesterday. The committee members present were Tao Baichuan, Ma Junshuo, Chen Cunren, Jiang Pingfan, Zhu Yakui, Yan Esheng, Zhu Fojiu, Wu Zhengxiao, Li Wenjie, Fan CaiKui, and Yu Chuanding. Zhu Ping, Director of the Land Administration Bureau, and Wu Zunyi, Chief Secretary of the Housing Lease Management Committee, were also present, ready to provide explanations at any time for reference during the review. Wu Zhengxiao, Zhu Yakui, and Yu Chuanding were the first to speak, pointing out that the internal structure of the Housing Lease Management Committee was too unsound, and there were numerous malpractices in arbitrating disputes. Moreover, after mediation by the committee, disputes not only could not be resolved, but also led to litigation. However, the courts did not pay attention to such civil lawsuits and often dragged on for six months or a year. In addition, the decisions of the Housing Lease Management Committee could not be enforced and were often overturned by the courts. Therefore, the committee has no credibility and is in name only. The parties involved in the dispute have great doubts about the fairness of the committee's decisions, so the committee should strengthen its organization to make itself sound. Senator Ma Junshuo continued to say: The Housing Lease Management Committee was established according to Article 23 of the Wartime Lease Regulations, but Article 24 of the regulations stated that the regulations would expire six months after the war. The committee has lost its legal basis, so the revision of the Housing Lease Management Regulations and the handling of dispute methods should be discussed carefully. Furthermore, the committee's rulings on housing disputes conflict with the courts. If the existence of this institution is still needed in the city, the legal aspect must be considered first, and it is recommended that the central government complete the legislative process in the future. Senator Ma also said that the committee's past mediation was too hasty, and it was done solely by the section chief or commissioner, resulting in many malpractices. If arbitration is still needed in the future, a collegial system must be adopted. Yan Esheng raised the question of whether the committee needs to continue to exist because it is a matter for administrative agencies. Therefore, Senator Tao Baichuan asked the third group, and learned that the third group's review opinion was that housing disputes can first be mediated by the district office, and if mediation fails, then the lease management committee will arbitrate. Senator Yan believed that since the third group had already decided this way, this case could be temporarily retained and decided after a joint review with the third group. Senator Ma believed that this was purely a legal basis issue, and the tenth group could not give up. Senator Zhu Fojiu said that the City Council has the right of initiative. If necessary, it can create a separate special law, and then, with the chairman's approval or through the legislative process, it can be applied with priority. Therefore, the first decision is whether it needs to exist. Senator Ma said that the nature of the city's separate laws belongs to orders, and orders must not conflict with central laws. Therefore, whether the committee continues to exist must first be determined by whether it has a legal basis and whether its rules and regulations conflict with the law. Senators Ma and Zhu quoted extensively and debated for a long time. Later, Director Zhu Ping stood up and stated that there are still many housing disputes in the city, and the committee is still needed in fact. If there is no problem with the abolition, the regulations can be discussed. Because it was late, three principles were set first, and other issues will be decided after a joint review and discussion with the third group. The three principles are (1) The mediation of the district office can be decided by the parties to the dispute themselves. (2) Arbitration shall adopt a five-person collegial system: one person from the municipal government, the court, and the police bureau, and two impartial local persons. The local impartial persons shall be proposed by the Mountain Council with a considerable number, and the chairman shall draw lots to decide two persons temporarily. (3) The revised draft shall be drafted by the Housing Lease Management Committee itself.

Regarding Police Security 72

The Second Review Committee. Yesterday afternoon, they reviewed proposals related to police security, dividing them into four major categories: 1. Volunteer police, self-defense forces, and security corps issues. 2. Firefighting work issues. 3. Issues related to improving police efficiency. 4. Matters that the police bureau should establish and implement. During the review of each proposal, Mr. Jiang Huaisu expressed the most opinions.

At the beginning of the city's victory, there was an original organization of security corps, but it was later abolished because the central government issued a clear order to abolish security corps in various places. All committee members believed that there was no need to restore it. As for the volunteer police, they were established in accordance with central laws and regulations to supplement the inadequacy of the police, which was definitely needed and should be strengthened. With winter defense approaching, the security work in the suburban security areas of the city is particularly important. To supplement the lack of police force, self-defense forces should be organized. This is a major focus of civil affairs work and has a legal basis. The committee members concluded that the security corps need not be restored, the volunteer police should be retained, and self-defense forces should be organized separately.

Firefighting work is related to the safety of citizens and should be strictly inspected. The ethics of firefighters is even more important and cannot be ignored. However, there is no firefighting item in this year's municipal budget. After a joint review by the committees, it was believed that the municipal government should be requested to stipulate a firefighting budget, strengthen firefighting equipment, and improve the work efficiency of firefighters.

Regarding the proposal to improve police efficiency, the review committee members believed that it is necessary to thoroughly eliminate the legacy of the former patrol rooms and establish a new police model. The police serve the people and should be polite to the common people. To improve the quality of police officers, it is stipulated that they must be junior high school graduates, and the treatment of police officers should be increased, with the lowest grade paid by appointment.

As for the matters that the police bureau should establish and reform, the most important and urgent matters are divided into three categories: investigating and banning private prostitutes and opium. Strengthening traffic control and eliminating pickpockets and petty thieves. All were approved in principle and the municipal government was requested to handle them separately.

Celebrating the Supreme Leader's Sixtieth Birthday; Mobilizing the Public to Prepare an Organization 73

The Seventh Review Committee. Yesterday, the review of proposals on social relief and labor was held, with a total of eleven people attending. Chairman Tang Shichang decided on the review method, and summarized all the proposals into fourteen categories. The conveners will prepare preliminary review opinions and submit them to the next review meeting for final decision. The proposal to prepare for the Chairman's Sixtieth Birthday celebration was also reviewed and passed. Because Speaker Pan and 39 others believe that since the Chairman launched the Northern Expedition, he has been working diligently day and night. This year coincides with the Chairman's sixtieth birthday, so they specially proposed to the Municipal Council to mobilize public groups to organize a preparatory committee to celebrate the Supreme Leader's sixtieth birthday and establish a permanent memorial to show respect for virtue and reward merit.

The fourteen categories of proposals are listed below: 1. Suppressing and stabilizing prices and rationing issues (4 items). 2. Labor-management issues (3 items). 3. Social welfare issues (1 item). 4. Relief issues (7 items). 5. Labor compulsory service (1 item). 6. Promoting the New Life Movement (3 items). 7. Farmers' welfare issues (2 items). 8. Cooperative enterprises (2 items). 9. Unemployment issues (3 items). 10. Women and children relief issues (4 items and 1 temporary motion). 11. Compensation for war losses and relief issues (1 item). 12. Labor welfare (9 items). 13. Implementation issues of the resolutions of the Provisional Council (2 items). 14. Petition from workers in the hotel industry (1 item).

A Solemn Appeal at the Council Meeting; Requesting the Recovery of Hong Kong, Kowloon, and Macau; The Owner of Hardoon Garden Has Agreed to Turn it into a Park 74

The last item on the agenda of the general meeting was to discuss several temporary motions.

Zhou Feicheng and more than 20 others jointly proposed that the municipal government contact the owner to lease Hardoon Garden and open it as a park for citizens to relax. The discussion concluded that because the Public Works Bureau had already contacted this matter and the owner had also expressed his consent, it was decided to hand it over to the Fifth Review Subcommittee for discussion.

The mayor submitted a proposal to extend daylight saving time to the end of October to save electricity, but the councilors strongly opposed it. The reason is that the time is near the Frost's Descent, and if daylight saving time is extended again, electricity may not be saved, but there will be many inconveniences for daily life and work. Feng Youzhen specifically mentioned the impact of daylight saving time on the morning newspaper publication time of the news industry. Finally, it was decided that this case would not be approved, and how to save electricity would be handed over to the Fifth Subcommittee for review.

The review of the municipal government's policy report was resolved to be jointly responsible by the conveners of each group.

The finale is often the most exciting. Wang Xianqing shouted out the call to "recover Hong Kong" in a solemn tone. He said: "Today there is a piece of news in the newspaper saying that the Hong Kong government spokesman does not recognize Kowloon City as Chinese territory. From Kowloon to Hong Kong, the phenomenon of Shanghai funds fleeing to Hong Kong is very serious. Recently, the Hong Kong dollar has risen, which has also stimulated the Shanghai market. Moreover, Hong Kong is a base for smuggling and tax evasion of foreign goods, which is an alarming economic loophole. Hong Kong residents are all Chinese citizens, and we should petition the national government to quickly negotiate and recover Hong Kong."

Councilors enthusiastically responded to his proposal and further mentioned another "tumor," Macau, and other places occupied such as Xinjiang, Mongolia, and Tibet, all of which should be recovered. Finally, the speaker summarized the opinions and decided to petition the national government to actively negotiate the recovery of Hong Kong, Kowloon, Macau, and other lands ceded or leased by unequal treaties, in order to benefit the integrity of the territory.

The group's review work has now been initially completed.

Suggesting the Central Government Adopt a Cash Guarantee System 76

The Fourth Review Committee held its second meeting yesterday at the Municipal Chamber of Commerce. The committee members Wang Xianqing, He Chengfu, Hong Fumei, Zhou Lianze, Huang Zhenshi, Yao Baozhen and others attended. The meeting was still chaired by Wang Xianqing. Two proposals were reviewed: The first proposal suggested that the central government abolish the current employee guarantee method and adopt the "Special Cash Guarantee System" that has been effectively tested by the Guangdong Provincial Bank, ordering government financial institutions to implement it as soon as possible in order to eliminate corruption cases and establish a sound guarantee system.

Wang Xianqing reported on the advantages of the cash guarantee system: (1) mutual supervision; (2) increasing savings; (3) due to the payment of the guarantee deposit, it has the effect of recovering legal currency; (4) it can also solve the difficulty of not being able to find a guarantor with a better reputation. Subsequently, other committee members expressed their opinions. The final review opinion was to submit it to the general meeting for approval. However, regarding the detailed methods and clauses of the system, it was proposed that Zhou Lianze conduct further research. The second proposal was the eight proposals submitted by the Municipal Chamber of Commerce in an official letter. The review opinion was to submit it to the general meeting for approval and recommend it to the Central Bank.

Horse Racing Issue; Opinions Are Still; Three Three Two Two 81

Later, Wang Jian'e raised a fundamental question. He said: "The Mayor's submission said that 'regarding horse racing, we must first ask whether it is purely horse racing or involves selling lottery tickets? If lottery tickets are sold, we can ask the municipal government to submit it to the Judicial Yuan to ask whether it is gambling according to Article 266 of the Criminal Law. If it conflicts with central laws and regulations, this case does not need to be discussed at all. ' "However, the opinions of the councilors were still mixed, and the more they discussed, the less clear they became. The scope was too large, and the result was still a decision to discuss it at the next review meeting.

Hangzhou's Major Theft Case Solved; Fang Zhengyuan is the Manager of the Pawnshop; The Victims are All Senior Officials and Celebrities 83

[Our Newspaper] Since last winter, no less than 20 "night theft" cases have occurred continuously in Hangzhou, but the targets of the thieves are all senior officials in the military and political circles, as well as lawyers and celebrities in the banking and business circles. For example, Shangguan Yunxiang, Deputy Commander of the Third War Zone Command, Xuan Tiewu's Hangzhou residence, Commander of the Songhu Garrison, Jin Runquan, President of the Bank of China, Chen Yanru, Councilor of the Third War Zone Command, Hu Xiwu, Director of the Investigation Office of the Zhejiang Provincial Security Command, lawyers Ye Wei, Zhao Jianxin, and others, all lost gold, silver, jewelry, coral, agate, gold watches, and diamond rings. Among them, Shangguan Yunxiang's residence was stolen of more than 4 million yuan in cash, and Commander Xuan's residence was stolen of sable coats, gray coats, fox coats, and coral Buddha hand jade bracelets. In addition, the Commercial Press, Shulianji Fan Shop, Baja Leather Shoe Store, Yanling Printing Factory, Hengsheng Paint Store, and Pan Wenbin, nephew of Division Commander Pan Guogang, Zhang Huchen, Technical Officer of the Public Works Bureau, Wang Sudan, etc., were all victims. Later, the Hangzhou Municipal Police Bureau arrested a receiver of stolen goods and seized ornaments and other items. According to the confession, the main culprit Fang Zhengyuan, the general manager of Shanghai Jifeng Pawnshop, was apprehended. According to Fang's confession, a part of the stolen goods was in his house at 314 Fuxing Middle Road in Shanghai. Therefore, the Hangzhou Police Bureau ordered Detective Ye Jianzhong to come to Shanghai with Fang under escort yesterday morning with official documents. Together with the police of the Taishan Branch, they secretly went to Fang's residence, arrested Fang's wife, Qiu (from Hubei, 36 years old), and his son, Guobin (19 years old), and seized a large suitcase of stolen goods such as "silver-clad gold" ornaments. It was then learned that another major criminal in the case was hiding at 52 Huangpi Road, so they went again and arrested Xiong Chuan and Zhang Xingwu (both from Hubei). The suspects and stolen goods were detained in the police station, awaiting escort back to Hangzhou for investigation.

US Military Tribunal Tries German War Criminals; No Infringement on Chinese Sovereignty; Prosecutor Sternly Refutes Defense Lawyer's Argument; Intense Dispute Over Whether to be Restricted by the German Surrender Instrument 84

[Our Newspaper] Yesterday, when the US military tribunal tried the German "Ehard Special Service Bureau" war criminals, defense lawyer Yang Linzhi launched a fierce attack in court, saying that the trial was illegal. Lawyer Yang said: Before the Judicial Yuan officially expresses its consent, even if there is an agreement between the US and Chinese governments, it cannot take effect. Therefore, the US military has no right to try these 23 German expatriates at all. He also claimed that, to his knowledge, the Judicial Yuan had never formally expressed its consent on this matter. Yang also cited the words of former US President Roosevelt, saying that the principle of trying war criminals should be that war criminals should be tried by the free government of the place where they committed the crime. Yang said: Germans had lost their consular jurisdiction in 1924 and had since been subject to Chinese law. However, Yang said that he did not object to the US military trying Japanese war criminals.

Lawyer Jiang Yiping, who defended defendant Baron Pugaman, also joined Yang's protest. After reciting the US military's regulations on the trial of war criminals one by one, he said that the defendant had not committed any of the items in these regulations.

German and Japanese are One and Indivisible

At this point, the chief prosecutor of the military tribunal, Major O'Connor, refuted, saying that the German expatriates protected by Chinese law refer to ordinary merchants and civilians, not those who come to China as enemies of China. He said that the defendants were all war criminals arrested in the war zone, which is different from ordinary criminals. O'Connor also said: The US military is stationed in China, having fulfilled its due obligations, and should also enjoy certain privileges. In response to Yang's claim that the US military came to China purely to defeat the Japanese army, O'Connor retorted that Germany and Japan were one and indivisible. The decision to try the defendants was originally to maintain world peace, that is, to ensure that there would be no third world war.

In response to Yang's claim that the trial of war criminals was an infringement of Chinese sovereignty and had aroused resentment among the Chinese people, O'Connor retorted that if the United States and China were to switch places, the United States would be very willing for Chinese military tribunals to try war criminals in the United States. The establishment of this US military tribunal was with the full consent of the Chinese government, and no protest from the Chinese government has been heard since the trial of Japanese war criminals. He said: If the Chinese army is also invited to the United States by the US government, as the Chinese government is doing to the US military now, if the Chinese troops stationed in the United States want to try war criminals, not only will it not arouse resentment from the American people, but it will definitely arouse the support of the American people.

Four Suspects Arrested in Peiping

O'Connor denied the claim of the defendant's defense lawyer that the US military was dissatisfied with the Chinese military tribunal, but said that he himself had heard that the Chinese military tribunal lacked talents, and suggested that Lawyer Yang, who is eloquent and eloquent, might as well show his talents in the Chinese military tribunal.

In response to Yang's claim that the defendants were overseas Chinese living in China and should be protected by Chinese law, O'Connor retorted that they were all enemies of the United States and China and could not be compared with ordinary overseas Chinese. Moreover, it was the puppet government presided over by Wang Jingwei who recognized them as official overseas Chinese.

Another defense attorney argued for the release of the defendants because they were not under the jurisdiction of the German Commander-in-Chief and therefore should not be restricted by the German instrument of surrender. The dispute was fierce, and it was not concluded until the adjournment. The hearing is scheduled to continue at 8:00 a.m. on Tuesday.

At the opening of the court yesterday, O'Connor announced that four more suspects in the case had been arrested in Beiping. They are currently detained in Chinese military institutions and will be transferred to justice soon.

Teenager Falls Victim to Scam When Buying Radio 88

[Our Newspaper] Liang Shixun, a 24-year-old from Guangdong, does coal business. On the 5th of this month, he opened a room at No. 322 Yuandong Hotel on Tibet Road and met two Westerners. The two Westerners used the sale of radios as a reason to lure him in. Liang was fooled. At 11:00 p.m. on the 15th, he went to the room opened by the Westerners at No. 512 of the hotel, paid 500,000 in cash, and agreed to pay the remaining 100,000 on the 16th to take delivery of the goods. At 10:00 a.m. yesterday, Liang sent the remaining 100,000 yuan to the Westerners because the appointment had expired. After one of the Westerners received the money, he falsely claimed that he would go to Hongkou to pick up the goods together. When they arrived at the entrance of a lane on Wuchang Road, the Westerner asked him to wait a moment. After more than an hour, he did not see him return. Liang knew he had been deceived and rushed back to report the situation to the Laozha Branch, requesting investigation. The police bureau learned that the two Westerners were indeed unemployed vagrants who lived by fraud. They are now being strictly arrested and brought to justice.

Severe Sentence in the Case of Chopping Husband and Dismembering Body: Zhan Zhou Still Sentenced to Death · The Defendant's Only Defense Was Lack of Premeditation · High Court Opened Trial Yesterday Afternoon and Concluded in One Hearing · 89

[Report from Our Newspaper] The sensational Jiangyuan Lane blood case in Shanghai during the enemy-puppet period – Zhan Zhou chopped her husband Zhan Yunying, and afterwards dismembered the body into sixteen pieces, packed them into a box, and attempted to destroy the evidence. The crime was discovered by the second landlord, Wang Xieyang, who reported it to the police. The female criminal Zhan Zhou was sentenced to death by the puppet court at the time. (Photo of Zhan Zhou taken by China Press during the hearing) The defendant refused to accept the sentence and was appealing to the puppet supreme court. Victory came, and the judgment was declared invalid, so the Municipal High Procuratorate re-investigated and prosecuted. Yesterday at 2:30 PM, the trial opened at the High Court on North Zhejiang Road, and it was concluded in one hearing. The defendant was immediately sentenced to death again.

(Before the Trial) Zhan Zhou submitted a petition to the High Court, requesting the revocation of the original judgment of the pseudo-first instance and a reduced sentence in accordance with Articles 273, 249, and 57 of the Criminal Law. The appeal was drafted by pro bono defense lawyers Chen Xia and Shi Baixiu, and the main points, facts, and reasons for the appeal are as follows.

(Main Points): The occurrence of this case was out of righteous indignation. It was a temporary motive in a state of confusion, without deep thought or premeditation. The original trial mistakenly regarded the purchase of a kitchen knife as definite proof of premeditation. The dismemberment was a cruel act. The severe sentence of death is difficult to accept.

(Facts): After marrying Zhan Yunying, although he was violent and quarrelsome, she could still endure it. Since the fall of Shanghai, he became addicted to gambling and neglected his proper business. He also opened an escort agency, colluding with the enemy and puppets day and night, enticing respectable men and women, and harming public morals. He refused to care for the family's livelihood, returning home once or twice a month, always after midnight (with enemy-puppet passes), and sweeping away pledges whenever he left. Any slight persuasion would result in violent beatings. In October of the 33rd year [of the Republic], feeling that life was meaningless, she swallowed Lysol and attempted suicide to end her life. Fortunately, she was discovered by a female tenant living on the terrace and rushed to Hongren Hospital on Xinzha Road for emergency treatment and survived. Ten days later, she was discharged from the hospital. Although her husband knew this, he did not show any compassion and abandoned her as before, making life even more difficult. She invited neighbors to gather and help fund her efforts, selling stewed pork and other items on the street to make ends meet. So, she bought a kitchen knife, cutting board, and bamboo basket, intending to start a business. However, her husband found out when he returned home at night and stole the working capital, causing her plans to fail. She then earned a living by embroidering and sewing for others. On the morning of March 20 of the 34th year [of the Republic], her husband returned at 3 AM. They argued and fought for about two hours, then fell asleep from exhaustion. She awoke from a nightmare at dawn. After urinating in a daze, she saw a kitchen knife nearby. Suddenly, she felt that her husband was harming the country and the people, so she acted on impulse and cut off his head. Realizing the enormity of her crime, she dismembered the body and packed it into a box, intending to carry it out and discard it. However, she sat blankly on the bed, unsure of what to do. The second landlord, Wang Xieyang, saw blood flowing downstairs, discovered the crime, and reported it to the police. This is the fact of the case.

(Reasons): The appellant’s husband opened an escort agency and colluded with the enemy and puppets, harming the country and the people. It was a temporary act of righteous indignation and intolerable provocation that led to the murder of her husband. Although the law is unforgiving, the circumstances are pitiable. According to Article 284, Section 1, Item 1 of the old Criminal Law, premeditation is required to constitute the crime of murder. Therefore, the act of killing must be based on the result of deep deliberation, and there must be a definite plan before implementation. If the intent to kill is decided on the spur of the moment, even if there is a long-standing feud, it is only a distant cause of the intent to kill and cannot be equated with intentional homicide. Therefore, it is inappropriate to impose the penalty for murder (see Precedent No. 2097, Shang Zi, 21st Year). This case was indeed a temporary decision, without any premeditation. The original judgment was based solely on conjecture to create a case of premeditated murder, which is not in accordance with legal principles. Furthermore, the dismemberment was to destroy evidence and cannot be compared to cruel acts such as heart-ripping or abdominal incision. Therefore, it only constitutes the crime under Article 249, Section 1, and Article 273 of the Criminal Law. The motive and purpose of the crime were decided on the spur of the moment, without deep deliberation or premeditation. The repeated provocations suffered by the appellant were intolerable for a weak woman, causing her to react impulsively. There was no other deliberate intention. Her difficult living conditions and lack of education are all in accordance with the provisions of Article 57 of the Criminal Law for mitigation. She humbly requests that she be granted leniency and a lighter sentence, which would be a great act of kindness.

(Zhou) is currently detained in the Women's Prison of the Shanghai Prison in Tilanqiao. Before the court session yesterday, she was specially brought to the High Court on North Zhejiang Road, wearing a blue cloth short shirt and trousers prisoner's uniform, with a white number [226] embroidered on her chest, and gray cloth closed-toe shoes on her bare feet. Her original long hair had been cut to ear length. She was short and had a pale face. At that time, the courtroom was crowded with spectators, mostly housewives. At 2:30 PM, Judge Zhang Qinglan, along with Judges Wang Kequan and Zhu Chengzan, Prosecutor Jiang Gongliang, and clerks, arrived and took their seats. They immediately ordered the bailiffs to bring up Zhan Zhou. They first asked her age, native place, and address. She replied: 31 years old, Danyang native, residing at No. 85, Lane 432, Xinchang Road, Jiangyuan Lane. After the prosecutor read out the indictment, the questioning began. Judge: Did you kill your husband at 3 AM on the night of March 20, 34th year? Answer: It was at dawn. I suddenly woke up and got up to urinate. I saw a knife in the drawer of a small cabinet next to the toilet, and I took the knife and killed him. Judge: Was your husband asleep or awake at this time? Answer: Awake. Judge: Was he sleeping facing in, facing out, on his back, or on his stomach? Answer: I don't remember clearly. Judge: Where was the first cut? Answer: I don't know. I was confused at this time and didn't know anything. Judge: Did your husband shout when you killed him? Answer: Sir, I don't know if he shouted or not. I was confused. Judge: Why did you kill your husband? Answer: It wasn't premeditated. It was a matter of the moment. He was usually bad-tempered. He ate, whored, gambled, and often ran the escort agency. If I asked him for living expenses, he would beat me. We were married for nine years without any affection.

(In Court) Judge: Then you could have divorced? Answer: I don't understand the law. My husband helped others say that he wouldn't give me living expenses and would let me have affairs, so he wouldn't have to pay me alimony when we divorced. Judge: Why did you chop him into sixteen pieces? Answer: After I killed him, it seemed like someone was telling me in my ear to chop him up, chop him up. Judge: Have you read "Ling Kong Shu"? Answer: No. Judge: Who else is in your family? Answer: No one. Judge: No one on your mother's side? Answer: No one on my mother's side, and no relatives on Zhan's side either. The judge then asked: Do you have a relationship with Little Ningbo? Answer: No, not at all. Judge: Why did you admit it before? Answer: I was forced to confess by torture at the police station. I had no choice and couldn't make my own decisions. Judge: You previously confessed that Little Ningbo gave you money to buy the kitchen knife? Answer: No. Judge: Did Little Ningbo tell you to kill him? Answer: He never said that. Judge: How could you, alone, kill Zhan Yunying, such a tall man? Answer: My soul wasn't in my body. I was possessed. When I killed him, I didn't treat him like a person, but like killing something else. Judge: Was the light on when you killed him? Answer: No. Judge: Did you have an affair with He Damazi, who lived in the front building? Answer: No affair, just some money. The judge immediately asked: Why are you now reversing all your previous confessions? Answer: I've always said this. Judge: Did He Damazi help you when you killed him? Answer: No. Judge: Then why did he run away afterwards? Answer: Someone from the countryside asked him to bring pancakes back, so he went back to the countryside.

(The Questioning) ended here. The presiding judge asked Zhou: Answer: Please, sir, I didn't do it intentionally. I was really confused for a moment, possessed. Please, sir, grant me a chance to live. Then the debate began, first with the prosecutor's argument, followed by the defense lawyer's response. (The reasons are detailed in the appeal). The presiding judge announced the end of the debate and waited for the court to deliberate before announcing the verdict on the spot. It was 3:05 PM. The defendant was temporarily taken away. The spectators discussed the matter animatedly, and the atmosphere was very tense. At 3:12 PM, the judges returned to the court and brought up the defendant. The presiding judge stood up and read the main text of the judgment: Zhan Zhou is sentenced to death for murder, deprived of public rights for life, and the kitchen knife is confiscated. The defendant wanted to argue more after hearing the verdict, repeatedly saying "not intentional." The court waved to stop her and told her that if she did not accept the verdict, she could apply for review to the Supreme Court in Nanjing within ten days after receiving the verdict. The defendant was then taken away by the bailiffs and detained.

It is noted that American lawyer Courtenay and several Japanese lawyers were retained on behalf of the defendant at this trial.

(Left) Kawashima, sentenced to hanging (Right) Matsuda, sentenced to seven years of labor (United Press Photo)

Shen Ke Sues United Press for Libel · Foreign Journalists Oppose Our Acceptance · Telegrams Sent to U.S. Secretary of State and Wu Dingchang · Requesting Revocation Through Appropriate Legal Procedures 90

[City News] The Foreign Correspondents' Club of China yesterday telegraphed U.S. Secretary of State Byrnes and Wu Dingchang, Director of the Bureau of Civil Affairs of the Chinese National Government, to strongly protest the Chinese court's acceptance of the case of Shen Ke, a national of a former enemy state currently being tried for war crimes, against Maitland, manager of the United Press China bureau, for defamation. The telegram to Director Wu Dingchang urged him to [fully consider the significant implications of the case], because foreign journalists believe that this case seriously damages freedom of the press and threatens their safety and personal freedom, and requested [revocation based on appropriate Chinese legal procedures]. Both telegrams pointed out that Shen Ke accused Maitland of defaming him in his news reports by stating that he was a Nazi spy, but in fact, these reports were based on official announcements from the U.S. military authorities. The foreign correspondents pointed out that Shen Ke has been deemed a [despicable] Nazi, and the Chinese government has decided to deport him. Legal authorities say that in this situation, he should have been deprived of his public rights long ago.

Xue Gengxin · Deeply Sinful 92

Xue is currently 36 years old and a native of Shanghai. The indictment states that the defendant was formerly a translator in the Malong Squad of the French Concession Police and was promoted to inspector-general after the war of resistance. He colluded with Sheng You to transport opium and used the [Malong Squad] to help the enemy arrest our underground comrades. On August 1, 32nd year [of the Republic], the puppet government took back the Shanghai concessions, and the defendant served as inspector-general and chief of the economic section of the puppet Third Police Bureau, then rose to become chief of the Meilan District Branch Bureau, deputy chief of the Huangpu Branch Bureau, and deputy director of the Special High Department of the puppet Police General Bureau. He also used the name of the Japanese Goto, director of the Special High Department, to forcibly purchase materials from various manufacturers at low prices and sell them on the black market for profit. According to reports from Qi Zaiyu and others, secret workers of the Military Intelligence Bureau in Shanghai, in the 29th year [of the Republic], the Shanghai West Special Operations organization lacked henchmen in the French Concession, so they won over the defendant and paid him a stipend. He also fought with Police Inspector Li to establish the Criminal Eighth Station to assist the enemy and puppets in arresting our underground comrades. The case was adjourned for further hearing.

Zhao Riliang, a translator for the Special High Department of the puppet police bureau, was originally sentenced to eight years. The defendant appealed, and the case was remanded for retrial. Trucks Soliciting Passengers · Rickshaws Severely Affected · Police Bureau Orders All Branches to Crack Down 93

[Report from Our Newspaper] Due to the lack of public transportation in the city and the high prices of rickshaws, large trucks carrying passengers have emerged, stopping at fixed locations and soliciting business, especially in the Hongkou and Zhabei areas. The fares are very cheap, with the highest fare being only 500 yuan. After the trend of trucks carrying passengers became popular, it not only hindered traffic but also violated the Public Works Bureau's automobile management regulations. The rickshaw business has also been severely affected. Now, in order to maintain their livelihood, they have submitted a petition to the Police Bureau yesterday, requesting a crackdown. It is said that the Police Bureau has ordered all branches to implement it starting today.

Bathhouse Labor Dispute Rages · Dozens of Businesses Vandalized 94

[Report from Our Newspaper] Although the bathhouse labor-management dispute was mediated by the authorities, the veteran workers did not accept it. After the vandalism that occurred at the Xinquan Pool on Fuxing Middle Road the night before last, dozens of bathhouses, both large and small, were vandalized yesterday afternoon throughout the city.
