Heavenly Soldiers and Generals Flying All Over the Sky: Paratrooper Drill in the Capital 146

— Nanjing, 6th, Yang Yanbing

At the reception for reporters hosted by Chief of General Staff Chen of the Ministry of National Defense, the reporter received a report from another colleague that the Paratrooper General Team would hold its first grand exercise in Nanjing the next day. This valuable clue excited the reporters too much. Quietly thinking about tomorrow's wonderful festival, and at the same time, guessing whether they would let us look at the "heavenly soldiers and generals" descending to occupy the land from the air? The mind was concentrated and the spirit soared, and the whole night was spent in turmoil.

Early in the morning of the 5th, the reporter woke up in the roar of engines, and looked at his watch, it was already 7:20. Hurried, hurried, he rushed to complete the entire grooming and housekeeping in three minutes. He took a car and desperately went to the gathering place at Xinjiekou. At this time, there were not many people on the street. News vendors shouted along the street. When the car passed Zhongzheng Road, I saw the cars of colleagues driving towards Zhonghua Gate one by one. The car drove faster after leaving Zhonghua Gate. The reporter was in the closest car and was the first to arrive at the review location of the Paratrooper General Team, and couldn't help but be extremely excited!

At this time, I could see rows and rows of paratroopers neatly arranged on the large parade ground. The reporter followed the signpost and went to the inspection ground. The receptionists greeted with smiles and gave out today's program. On the signature book, I discovered that Minister of National Defense Bai Chongxi, General Jiansheng was also here. Minister Bai has been busy with military affairs, and I have not seen him for a long time. Being able to see his demeanor again today is another gain from participating in the grand ceremony.

At 8:00 AM sharp, Minister Bai led Lieutenant General Ma Chongliu, Lieutenant General Xu Tingyao, and more than 30 inspection officers and entourage forward to the inspection ground. At this time, Commander Ma of the Paratrooper General Team had rushed from the defense area in Suzhou to accompany the inspection. Minister Bai nodded frequently as he walked to each row, appearing very happy. Afterwards, he visited the internal affairs, parachute folding practice, asked many questions, and gave instructions. When visiting the weapons, General Ma Chongliu explained the latest American rifle to Minister Bai. Minister Bai picked up the gun and made an anchoring motion, and smiled at the reporter: "I joined the army at the age of twenty, and have always been accustomed to using a rifle. Today, I picked up this American rifle, and it is completely different from the rifle I used thirty years ago. Scientific progress is truly overwhelming."

The Growth of Seedlings, a Sign of National Rebirth 147

Immediately, he visited basic parachuting. The reporter thought that the growth of this seedling of national defense is a sign of the rebirth of the Republic of China. He excitedly asked Minister Bai about the future goals of paratrooper construction, and he told the reporter: "The Chinese paratroopers were established in 1943. In the past two years, the war exploits of attacking Hengyang, Danzhu, and Guilin were truly too great. We must make these batches of seedlings grow well. We are prepared to expand into many divisions and many armies to take on future national defense missions."... At 10:15, he visited battlefield psychological testing. A heated and wonderful scene unfolded on a field of several hundred meters. Dozens of soldiers practiced crossing the battlefield in a crossfire of landmines, artillery shells, and bombs. At this time, the firepower was dense, the sounds were continuous, and landmines and bombs exploded at the same time. The fireworks of red and green flares enveloped the Chen terrain. Dimly, I saw soldiers crawling forward on the field, as if facing a great enemy. Minister Bai asked the reporters several times, "Is the action good?" His words seemed to contain unlimited joy. Immediately, he visited. The combat exercises were also extremely impressive. Minister Bai said to the reporters during the proceedings: "Are there any reporters from the New China Daily today? We would be very welcome if they came to see us." This aroused a burst of smiles from the reporters.

At 11:30, the visit was over, and after a brief refreshment in the reception room, he took a car and returned to the city.

Air Force Parachuting, the Program Is Special and Wonderful 148

At 1:30 PM, at Ming Palace Airport, he visited Air Force parachuting. This was the most brilliant and unprecedented program in the capital. The emotions of the paratrooper soldiers were hotter than the scorching autumn sun. They were about to present the beautiful postures of combat in the skies over Guangdong, Luoding, Xijiang, and Hengyang to the millions of citizens and senior military officers in the capital. At this time, there were people everywhere inside and outside the Air Force Transportation Station. Commander-in-Chief of the Air Force, Lieutenant General Zhou Zhirou arrived the earliest. Minister Bai also came with his wife and two sons. Lieutenant General Ma Chongtian, Lieutenant General Xu Ting??, Lieutenant General Zhang Zhen, Police Chief Han Wenhuan, and a special car from the Ministry of National Defense loaded ten officials came. In addition, there were dozens of female relatives. Three large Model 47 aircraft faced the reviewing stand. The 36 soldiers participating in the parachuting were assigned to three special aircraft, No. 302, No. 297, and No. 296, with twelve people on each aircraft. When they were disembarking to board the plane, the reporter group seized the opportunity and requested to visit the plane. As a result, the nine reporters were divided into three groups, with three people on each aircraft. I walked into the aircraft door with joy and curiosity. After a while, the engine made a loud noise, and the aircraft slowly rose. It circled in the air first, and the commanding instructors Chen Zhonggui, Huang Kai, Wang Keqiu, and Yang Derun led the singing of "Paratrooper Song." Most of them had fought in Kaiping, Guangdong, and had risked their lives in the flames of war. Today they deserved to be proud. Looking down from the window again, the fields and streams were scattered like stars. The Yangtze River was like a belt, and Qingliang Mountain and Sun Yat-sen Mausoleum gradually passed by.

A Lily Drifting in the Air 149

After only about five minutes, we reached an altitude of one thousand feet. A series of rapid bells rang from the tail of the aircraft, indicating that this was the signal to start parachuting. Then a rubber man for measuring wind direction was pushed out of the aircraft door to test the wind direction. The people in the cabin quickly looked at the posture of the landing. The first person to perform on Aircraft No. 302, which the reporter was riding, was Instructor Bird Qifa, a captain. He made a ready-to-jump posture in front of the aircraft door. The two instructors next to him checked him. The aircraft made a large circle and had already reached above the Ming Palace. Captain Bird immediately jumped out of the aircraft door, and the two assistants were busy collecting the buckles. Everyone crowded to the aircraft door to watch. A beautiful lily was drifting in the air, slowly falling, and looked even more vivid, white, and beautiful in the sunlight. When the aircraft circled back and forth around the city and returned to the Ming Palace, the audience applauded continuously. After that, they jumped in groups of two and three. Each student opened the parachute three seconds after jumping out of the aircraft door. The diameter of the parachute was six feet. Lilies appeared in the clear sky, one after another. I couldn't help but salute the commanding instructor. When the fifth time they returned to the sky above the aircraft hangar, all twelve people had jumped. The driver, seeing that the mission was completed, headed towards the Ming Palace Airport to land. At this time, it was exactly 2:00 PM. The last time, twelve people landed simultaneously from two aircraft. The beautiful umbrellas were pure white, yellow, red, and green, slowly descending. What poetic works of art they were!

Finally, Minister Bai delivered a speech expressing his thoughts on the review: "These are the seedlings of our paratroopers. We must make them grow strong. Paratroopers are the newest type of scientific soldiers. We must build them up and coordinate with our national defense."

Black Sea Situation 150

— Our newspaper's Beijing-based reporter, Ding Weidong

Recently, the Black Sea situation has been very dangerous. The Soviet Union has formally proposed a demand for joint Soviet-Turkish defense of the Dardanelles Strait. They view it as a matter for the Black Sea nations, and do not want Britain, the United States, and France to participate in the negotiations. Britain, the United States, and Turkey, on the other hand, believe that this is an international issue, and any amendment to the Montreux Convention should be conducted through an international conference, and cannot be decided by the unilateral will of the Soviet Union. As of now, more than a million Red Army troops have gathered on the borders of the two countries, and a war of nerves is already underway! There is a chorus of resistance in the Turkish parliament. The United States has bluntly warned the Soviet Union that controlling the straits and controlling Asia could lead to war. The clouds of war seem to be looming again over the war-torn skies of Europe.

The political system of a country may change, the governing figures may change, but the historical background and geographical situation of a country will not change. Whether it is Tsarist Russia or the Soviet Union, the fact proves that the national aspirations of Russia will not change. Therefore, to understand the essence of the strait issue, it is better to seek it in Russian history than in grand diplomatic rhetoric.

"Constantinople World Hegemony" 151

The rise of modern Russia defeated two strong enemies in total. Under Peter the Great, he defeated Sweden, which dominated Northern Europe at that time, and obtained ports on the Baltic Sea. The "window" to the north was opened. In the south, Peter the Great's successor, Empress Catherine, repeatedly defeated Turkey, expanded its territory, and made Russia a Black Sea nation. Throughout the 19th century, Russia was committed to a southward policy, with the ultimate goal of obtaining Constantinople and controlling the Black Sea straits. In 1805, Napoleon of France dominated Europe, and defeated Russia on the plains of Poland, but in order to defend against Britain, he turned around and courted Russia, and the two sides signed the Treaty of Tilsit. The effect of this treaty was to divide the European continent into the spheres of influence of France and Russia. Western and Central Europe belonged to France, while Eastern and Northern Europe belonged to Russia. Everything went smoothly during the negotiations, but when the Russian Tsar mentioned Constantinople, Napoleon suddenly interrupted him and said heavily, "Constantinople? This is an issue of world hegemony!" The two sides negotiated repeatedly, but never reached an agreement. This unresolved issue eventually became the seed of the breakdown of French-Russian relations in 1812. From the Congress of Vienna to World War I, Balkan wars occurred frequently. In addition to ethnic hatred, the desire of Tsarist Russia to weaken Turkey and control the straits was an important reason.

The Straits Story: Endless Vicissitudes 152

At the beginning of World War I, in order to win over Russia and tie up German forces to prevent their concentration on the Western Front, Britain and France had agreed that after the war, Constantinople and the Black Sea Straits would be given to Imperial Russia as spoils of victory. St. Petersburg was overjoyed upon receiving this promise. In 1916, the Russian army suffered defeats on the Eastern Front, causing morale to waver. At the same time, due to Turkey's entry into the war, Russia was unable to receive supplies from Britain and France via the Black Sea route, putting it in a very difficult situation. At that time, the French ambassador to Russia (a historian and writer) saw lines of new Imperial Russian recruits in Petersburg during the snowy winter. These pitiful replacements were poorly clothed, some even barefoot. Due to a lack of rifles, some were even unarmed, struggling through the snow on their way to the front. The ambassador asked himself: How could Russia, in this critical situation, still have the confidence to continue fighting? His conclusion was, "The beautiful prospect of Constantinople is what guides them forward!"

Britain still holds the view that Turkey's attitude was quite hesitant during the First World War, and that its alliance with Germany was due to a chance occurrence. On the eve of the war, Turkey had ordered warships from the British Admiralty, but once the ships were completed, the European war situation had already developed, and Britain kept the warships for its own use, causing displeasure in Turkey. When the war broke out, two German warships escaped the search of the British Navy, entered the Black Sea Straits, and docked in Constantinople. This series of events became the spiritual capital for Germany to win over Turkey. Later, during the war, under Churchill's advocacy, Britain launched the so-called "Dardanelles Adventure," which resulted in heavy casualties and a disappointing retreat. However, historians later argued that if this operation had succeeded, Turkey would have certainly surrendered, which would have accelerated the defeat of the Central European powers and ended the European war two years earlier! After the end of the European war, Turkey and Greece went to war. The Greek invading forces retreated from the Turkish interior all the way to the straits. The Turkish army pursued them northward and could have crossed the narrow strait to recover its old territory in Europe, but the British Navy blockaded the straits at that time, waiting in battle array. Churchill wrote vividly in his memoirs: "The Admiralty had absolute confidence that it could prevent the Turkish army from entering Europe purely through naval power." After the Treaty of Lausanne was established, Turkey obtained an opportunity for self-reliance, but the straits became an undefended area, leading to the relocation of the capital of the new Turkey. The historical lesson of this World War is enough to prove that the Black Sea Straits are the lifeline of Turkey's national defense. If the straits fall into the hands of another country, Turkey's independence will exist in name only!

Britain and the US Advocate Joint Control 153

In this war, Turkey responded to the crisis with vigilance and autonomy, ultimately avoiding being drawn into the vortex of war. Although it did not participate in the war, the entire country remained in a state of mobilization from June 1940 onwards. The American Lend-Lease Act was also applied to Turkey. According to the British-Turkish Mutual Assistance Agreement, if Turkey were attacked, British air force from bases in Africa could reach Turkish airspace within five minutes. Turkish air force bases were completely transformed by British and American experts to facilitate the stationing of the air forces of both countries at any time. In fact, although Turkey did not participate in the war, it shielded the Middle East and indirectly contributed significantly to the Allied nations. During this war, Turkey's relationship with Germany and the Soviet Union was quite delicate, and two incidents occurred that were never fully resolved. The first was the attempted assassination of the German ambassador to Turkey, von Papen, in the Turkish capital. Berlin said it was done by Soviet personnel with the aim of causing a Turkish-German war and facilitating the entry of the Red Army into Turkish territory. Moscow said it was done by German special agents with the aim of creating a pretext for German aggression. Turkey's attitude was one of silence, and the case was never solved. The second was Germany's publication of a batch of documents and maps related to the Soviet Union's territorial demands on Turkey, which caused a great uproar. Germany insisted that the materials came from the Soviet Union and were very reliable; while Moscow strongly condemned the Nazis for undermining Soviet-Turkish relations. Throughout the war, Turkey was cautious, fearing imminent disaster, and fundamentally distrusted both Germany and the Soviet Union. As soon as the war ended, the Soviet autonomous republics immediately demanded territory from Turkey, causing the Turkish authorities to maintain a large army and dare not demobilize!

At the Potsdam Conference, the Soviet Union formally proposed the demand for joint defense of the Dardanelles Straits. It based this on the principle of "international equality." Here, the so-called international referred to the three great powers of Britain, the United States, and the Soviet Union, and not to other countries. At the conference table, Stalin pointed to Churchill and said, "The Suez Canal is a vital waterway for your survival, and you have occupied and defended it." Then he pointed to Truman and said, "The Panama Canal is a vital waterway for your survival, and you have occupied and defended it; therefore, according to the principle of international equality, the Soviet Union has the right to demand the defense of the Black Sea Straits." Britain and the United States unanimously opposed this demand and advocated international control. Churchill said at the time: "If the straits become a Soviet naval base, only Russian ships will come out, and no British ships will go in!"

The Northern Bear Is Obsessed with the Ocean 154

In addition to fulfilling historical desires, the British and Americans have a new observation regarding the Soviet Union's obsession with controlling the straits, which is that the Soviet Union has developed a very deep interest in the ocean. By the Yalta Conference, Byrnes had already sensed this. Subsequent developments confirmed this. In the East, the Soviet Union had already acquired the Lushun naval base—the Gibraltar of the Yellow Sea. In the West, the Soviet Union supported Yugoslavia in acquiring ports on the Adriatic Sea. The port of Trieste is an important Central European seaport, and the shipbuilding facilities and skilled workers there could be utilized. Regarding Italy, it demanded one-third of the fleet and naval bases in North Africa. It was expected that it would demand a large portion of warships, merchant ships, and fishing boats from Japan as reparations. Joint control of the Black Sea Straits would allow the Soviet Union to become a Mediterranean power, developing its influence in Africa and the Near East. The Northern Bear also wanted to control the ocean, which, of course, conflicted with the interests of Britain and the United States, who regarded the ocean as their lifeline. In addition to other important political and military reasons, this is one of the motivations for Britain and the United States' firm support for Turkey.

Page 10

Crimes of Japanese War Criminals - From Our News Data Room - The Poisonous Executioner: Konoe Fumimaro 155

When the name of Konoe Fumimaro, the chief culprit of the invasion of China, is mentioned, all Chinese people gnash their teeth with hatred. Although he is dead, how can we allow such a vicious executioner to "die and be done with"?

Konoe's latent power in Japan was considerable: He was born in 1891 and raised under the care of Prince Saionji. He had attended the Paris Peace Conference with Saionji and had long inherited Saionji's mantle, joining the ranks of Japanese "elder statesmen." He organized organizations such as the Toyo Society and the Nanyo Society, secretly preparing to launch a war of aggression against China. After Hayashi Senjūrō stepped down, Konoe rose to form a cabinet and launched the "North China Incident" upon taking office, mobilizing three divisions and over a hundred aircraft to attack Peiping and Tianjin. On the one hand, he flaunted the so-called "Konoe Three Principles" and the "policy of non-expansion," causing incalculable losses to the Chinese army and people. However, his conspiracy was finally exposed under the guidance of our wise supreme leader in the War of Resistance. Following this, there was the so-called "Konoe Statement," which put forward the slogans of the "Greater East Asia New Order" and "long-term warfare," all of which were thoroughly refuted by our authorities, forcing him to announce the collapse of his cabinet.

In June 1940, seeing Germany's military successes in Europe, Konoe took office again to form a cabinet, completing the proud masterpiece of the "Japan-Germany-Italy Military Alliance." After the outbreak of the Soviet-German War, Matsuoka Yōsuke was dismissed, and the Konoe cabinet was reorganized, even more recklessly pursuing militarism, and the arrogance of the warlords was unparalleled. After Hiranuma Kiichirō was assassinated, Konoe's third cabinet collapsed again.

In summary, from his rise to his fall, he formed a cabinet three times. His first cabinet led to the Sino-Japanese War; his second cabinet colluded with Germany and Italy, leading to international isolation; after his third cabinet failed, Tōjō Hideki came to power, leading to the Pacific War.

Please see the following excerpt from Konoe's conversation with Wang Jingwei: "The Japanese government has repeatedly declared in its statements this year that it will thoroughly eliminate the anti-Japanese National Government by force, and at the same time is willing to work hand in hand with enlightened Chinese people to move toward the construction of the East Asian New Order. Japan, Manchukuo, and China will jointly realize good neighborly friendship, joint anti-communism, and economic cooperation." The Chinese people suffered greatly under Wang Jingwei's tyranny, much of which was Konoe's "achievement."

After the victory, Konoe suddenly appeared in a pro-British and pro-American posture, frequently courting the Allied forces, and promoted constitutional amendments, hoping to emerge again to form a cabinet. He even fantasized about coming to China to "apologize." But this could not cover up his heinous crimes. On December 6th of last year, Konoe was "at the top of the list" of war criminals to be arrested by MacArthur. Finally, on the morning of the 16th of that month, he committed suicide by taking poison, leaving behind a will that continued to make excuses, claiming: "In due time, there will be public opinion on right and wrong!" He can be said to have been unrepentant until his death.

Old Fascist: Hiranuma Kiichirō 156

Konoe's second cabinet collapsed because he could do nothing about the war expenses in China, the international atmosphere was bad, and the fascist military was dissatisfied. The one who succeeded him, shouldering the heavy responsibility of "creating a new order and maintaining permanent peace in East Asia," was Baron Hiranuma Kiichirō, who served as prime minister for only seven months.

Hiranuma was born in 1867 and graduated from the Law Faculty of Tokyo Imperial University. He served in the Ministry of Justice. In 1911, he was appreciated by Justice Minister Matsuda Masahisa and appointed Vice Minister of Justice. In 1912, he served as Prosecutor General of the Supreme Court for as long as eight years. In 1921, he was promoted to President of the Supreme Court. In 1923, when the Yamamoto cabinet was established, he served as Justice Minister, establishing an unshakable power in the judicial field. In 1924, he was appointed Privy Councilor, and in April of the following year, he was appointed Vice President of the Privy Council. In 1933, he served as President of the Privy Council.

Hiranuma was the leader of Japanese fascists. He founded the Shūyōdan (Cultivation Group), serving as its director, and in 1924, he founded the Kokuhonsha (National Foundation Society), serving as its president, advocating "Imperial Household Centralism" and publishing "Kokuhon" and "Kokuhon Shimbun." Its members included bureaucrats, military officials, nobles, and people from all walks of life. Suzuki Kisaburō, Tōgō Heihachirō, Gotō Shinpei, Araki Sadao, Koiso Kuniaki, Matsui Iwane, Kikuchi Takeo, and zaibatsu Ikeda Seihin, and bureaucrat scholar Yamakawa Kenjirō were all members of the society. He also collaborated with Araki Sadao, vigorously attacking the Seiyūkai, and tried several times to form a cabinet, but failed due to opposition.

In 1939, Hiranuma finally fulfilled his lifelong wish at the high age of 73, but within two months of taking office, he was heavily criticized from all sides. The cabinet became an appendage of the military, with no power to interfere in foreign policy, and everything was controlled by Army Minister Itagaki and Education Minister Araki. In August of the same year, he resigned. In 1940, he briefly served as Minister of the Interior, and later as Deputy Prime Minister. In 1945, he was reappointed President of the Privy Council.

On December 2nd of last year, Hiranuma was among the 59 war criminals ordered to be arrested by MacArthur. This 80-year-old fascist "meritorious official" was finally thrown into prison, awaiting trial by the International Tribunal.

Violent Black Dragon: Hashimoto Kingorō 157

Hashimoto Kingorō was originally a standard Japanese rōnin, but in the militaristic Japanese fascist government, he actually became a remarkable figure.

Hashimoto was the leader of the "Japan Youth Party" and the head of the "Black Dragon Society." He absurdly styled himself as a superior Nazi, once saying that "National Socialism and Fascism are like the stars and moon in the evening sky, which can only be adorned more clearly in the morning light of Great Japan." The famous writer John Gunther called him "the founder of the one-party idea, an extremely violent young military officer." Because of the support of his "Black Dragon Society" behind the scenes, he often lived in robbery, assassination, and espionage, creating his terrifying reputation.

When he served as an adjutant at the Turkish embassy in 1927, he was already obsessed with studying German and Italian Nazi politics. In 1936, due to the rise of his Youth Party, he formed a fascist government combining civil and military bureaucrats, and issued a declaration of the "Leaping Great Japan National System Outline" (also known as the Hashimoto Kingorō Declaration), shouting the slogans of "Emperor First" and "National Control and Management."

In 1937, he rejoined the army, commanding a fleet of warships to invade China, creating the horrific Nanjing Massacre, and directing the bombardment of the American gunboat "Panay" and the British gunboat "Ladybird." He authored numerous works, publishing articles in the "Taiyō Dai-Nippon" magazine and other publications, and giving public speeches. The book "The Inevitability of Reform," which has now been submitted to the International Tribunal as evidence, is his "masterpiece," revealing his immense joy when he drowned our soldiers in the Yangtze River, and his desire to drive out British and American forces in China to realize Japan's monopolistic plans. He also often used conspiracies to overthrow civil and military officials whom he considered to be "lacking in ambition." In 1940, he was also the founder of the Imperial Rule Assistance Association.

This lawless warlord has been tried in the Tokyo International Tribunal, and everyone hopes that this "Old Black Dragon" will be given the most severe punishment!

Isolated City in Northern Jiangsu: Hai'an 158

— Zhenjiang, 7th Dispatch, Wang Hanou

When the reporter and local merchants walked out of the earthen city of Hai'an, they saw large numbers of Communist leaflets and slogans scattered on the ground. Everyone was filled with fearful apprehension. According to one or two people with ulterior motives, they also saw militiamen secretly reconnoitering in the distant woods. Whether this was true or false, the fact that there was Communist activity as soon as one left the earthen city was indeed true. Moreover, before this, Hai'an had shown signs of being surrounded; at night, the sound of hand grenades and machine guns became a regularly performed rhythm. But the garrison and residents did not pay excessive attention to it, only calmly dealing with it with the word "calm," which is the only good way to deal with the Communist military strategy, and the only good way to adapt to the current environment. Because after the National Army opened the Tongyang Line, it needed some reorganization and deployment in preparation for the next phase of operations, and it did not extend northward. Each town along the highway did not have "satellite" strongholds. As soon as the Communist military launched a "counterattack," they immediately approached the city, and there was no better way than to resolutely defend it with deep trenches and high ramparts.

Neat fortifications

When the reporter was in the town, the bunkers and fortifications in the earthen city were built neatly. The 65th Division was stationed in the town, and everyone inside seemed to be engineers, able to work as plasterers. The brothers carried bricks and mixed mortar themselves to build bunkers. They lived in civilian homes, and each outpost had a short protective wall built in front of it. Obstacles were piled up on every street and alley, preparing for all street battles. These bricks and stones for building fortifications were dug up from road bricks in the back streets and alleys, wooden door panels were temporarily requisitioned from residents, and a small number of tile and wood craftsmen also participated in the work.

Grain storage and death defending

When Hai'an District Chief Wang Jingyi convened a meeting of citizens, he announced that the entire town's residents would collectively store 12,000 dan of grain in preparation for a month-long siege. Each guild would supervise each merchant, and each baojia chief would supervise each household, trying to search for and store grain until the quota of 12,000 shi was filled and the food supply was sufficient. When the reporter was in the town, the residents all received temporary passes, and went out of the city every day to buy rice and grass from nearby villages. The lowest price of new rice was once as low as 34,000 yuan, but soon rose again to 45,000 yuan per shi. Grass then rose to 89,000 yuan per dan, equal to the price of large wheat at 130 jin per shi. Many people chopped up old furniture for cooking fuel, which, although painful, was said to be more cost-effective than "buying at expensive prices."

Roads extend in all directions

The earthen city of Hai'an was built by the puppet army during the period of occupation, and cost a lot of civilian blood and sweat at that time. When the New Fourth Army "liberated" the area, because they felt that the area was "indispensable," this earthen city was not only not demolished, but also processed and repaired, until the Communist military withdrew from the town, it was intact. In addition, there were two moats inside and outside the city, which was fully suitable for the conditions of deep trenches and high ramparts. What "indispensable" relationship did Hai'an have? It is the transportation hub connecting the southeast, northwest, south road to Tong (zhou) Ru (gao), west road to Yang (zhou) Tai (county), east road to Peng (cha) Li (bao) into the sea, north road to Dong (tai) Yan (cheng), directly to Huai (yin) Hai (zhou), and all these lines can be reached by road these days. In short, Hai'an is the center of transportation. With it, one can control the overall situation. Without it, a large section of the highway line would be forced to be completely abandoned.

Democratic lawsuit

Han Guojun, the former governor of Jiangsu Province who was comparable to Wu Peifu during the War of Resistance, was born in the town. When the local area fell in 1930, Han took refuge in a northeast village. He was kidnapped by enemy troops sent to the village to force him to take a puppet post, but Han resolutely vowed his allegiance and was unyielding in the face of danger, eventually dying for his ideals. Han's style name was Zishi. The New Fourth Army's "Democratic Government" hypocritically renamed the town "Zishi County" to commemorate his labor, but because his daughter, Han Liuqi, was one of the local capitalists, she was also arrested and subjected to a "democratic lawsuit" when the struggle was launched this spring. It was not until the Battle of Northern Jiangsu was about to begin that she was released. Now Ms. Liuqi is also in the town presiding over the Joint Military-Civilian Affairs Office and the Chamber of Commerce, planning to restore local affairs.

Battle of Fengshan

Newspaper telegrams intensely report on Mount Lushan, but there is no Mount Lushan in Hai'an, nor is there a North Mount Lushan. It is probably a mistake for Fengshan in the northeast corner two miles away from the town. Fengshan is one of the three ponds and ten scenic spots in Hai'an. The scenery is beautiful and shaped like a phoenix. Climbing the peak can overlook the entire city. In order to control the war situation, both sides must swear to defend this high ground. Part of the temples on Fengshan were demolished by the Communist army, and the three ponds and ten scenic spots have already shown signs of incompleteness. The Communist military's method of destroying temples is indeed terrible. The Guangfu Temple in Hai'an is one of the 24 forests in Xiahe. The architecture is even more magnificent than the Jing'an Temple in Shanghai, and it was also torn apart by the Communist military. The "religious freedom" declared by the Communist military's "Democratic Government," I don't know where this statement went.

Residents waiting to be fed

Hai'an is currently an important place in the battle for North Jiangsu. The military and civilians are defending the city to the death. Although the offensive of the Communist military's 12 regiments has weakened and the situation has become looser, external transportation has not yet recovered, and all industries are in a state of suffocation. The citizens deal with war and life every day, and prices are surprisingly high. Since the National Army advanced to the present, they have not received any relief supplies. It was previously reported that the Jiangsu-Ningbo branch of the Relief Headquarters had 500 tons of flour shipped in, specifically to relieve the disaster areas of Jiang, Qu, and Hai, but the highway in the Qutang area was cut off, and it is temporarily difficult to transport it in. The general poor people are like "carp in a dried rut," looking forward with longing eyes.

The Common Disaster and Oppression of the Flood in Haizhou 159

— Special Dispatch from Haizhou by Our Newspaper, 3rd. Correspondent: Li Shangnong

Haizhou, in the past a remote corner, has become the heart of northern Jiangsu and the gateway to the coast since the opening of sea trade and the construction of the Longhai Railway. It is now a major hub for military, political, cultural, and economic activities in the Huaihai region. It boasts hundreds of miles of fertile fields producing soybeans and wheat in the front, vast salt fields in the rear, and the Tongyun Grand Port, a major hub for goods, attracting attention from both domestic and foreign sources.

Currently, all local military, political, cultural, and financial institutions are located in Xinpu, which is twelve Chinese miles from Haizhou City, resulting in unusually prosperous commerce. Land transportation includes the Longhai Railway, Qinghai Highway, and Huaihai Highway. Water transportation offers direct routes from Lianyungang to Shanghai, Qingdao, Guangdong, Dalian, Xiamen, and other places. The Yunyan River provides inland navigation to Qingjiang. Before the incident, the China National Aviation Corporation had an aviation station in Haizhou, with daily north-south flights landing to carry passengers and transport mail, making transportation quite convenient.

During March and April of spring, the refugees' only hope was that the Communist army would quickly withdraw from the Haizhou territory, allowing people to return home to harvest wheat. By the time the wheat turned yellow in May, refugees from the various counties of Haizhou had spontaneously organized homecoming teams to return home to harvest wheat. Unexpectedly, all the returning teams were driven back by the Communist army's guns and artillery, and the wheat they had planted was harvested and transported away by the Communist army.

The displaced refugees, seeing that the wheat had been reaped by the Communist army and their livelihood destroyed, although they received flour from the Relief Administration and local authorities made efforts to provide relief, it was a mere drop in the bucket. Everyone still suffered from hunger. Many refugees fled from Xinpu to the south of the Yangtze River to find a way out. There are still 44,706 refugees in Xinpu, which is more than one-half fewer than in the spring. These more than 40,000 refugees look forward to returning home every day, because autumn has already arrived, and they will soon need cotton clothes. If they cannot return home, it will be even harder to bear the cold and hunger.

Disrupting Transportation and Blocking Food Supplies

After occupying the county towns of Shu and Gan, the Communist army violated the ceasefire order in January, disrupting transportation and occupying Baitabu on the Longhai Railway, as well as westward locations. They forcibly conscripted young men, killed family members who evaded military service, and repeatedly attacked outposts outside Haizhou, such as Xinba and Zhangwu, as well as Gezhuang near the outskirts of Guanyun County, which was also frequently attacked by the Communist army.

Although the Communist army did not cease attacks on outposts surrounding Hai and Guan counties, the local militia, under the command of General Duan Linmao of the National Army, defended with composure. Each time the Communist army attacked, they suffered heavy blows. The National Army in Haizhou launched a movement to save one meal to provide relief to refugees in Hai and Xin, with the army and civilians loving each other like family, sincerely united to defend the Haizhou base of the Huaihai area. Seeing that Haizhou could not be captured, the Communist army strengthened its blockade policy. Because the grain-producing areas were occupied by them, what we defended was only the county towns of Dongguan and Xinpu, Lianyungang, and other suburban areas, with very little grain production. Since the food and fuel were blockaded by the Communist army, food prices soared, causing public panic about food, and other prices also rose.

Haizhou was blockaded by the Communist army on three sides, north, south, and west. Only the sea off Lianyungang to the east allowed for traffic in and out, with ships traveling to and from Qingdao, transporting cloth and sundries. If it were not for the seaport of Lianyungang, even breathing would have been suffocated.

Originally, there were 700 stores, companies, and salt businesses of various kinds in Xinpu, and commerce was very prosperous. After the city's new outskirts and the Longhai Railway were occupied and blockaded by the Communist army, commerce plummeted, and stores closed one after another. As commerce declined, industry also fell into decline. Other peddlers and small businesses were unable to operate due to the interruption of traffic. There were seven or eight thousand unemployed and idle people in Xinpu. Many unemployed and poor people did not have a single meal a day, and their faces were pale, filling the corners of the new city. Local government officials and school teachers, due to low salaries and high prices, mostly worked on empty stomachs, truly experiencing unspeakable suffering. The only people who lived happily were the uncaptured traitors, profiteers who made a fortune from the national crisis, and a few corrupt officials who profited from victory. The rest of the people lived in misery.

Digging Dikes and Releasing Water to Submerge Autumn Crops

Because the Communist army in the Huaihai area suffered defeats in the northern Jiangsu battles, they disregarded the lives of the people and dug up the dikes of the Shu and Yun canals. The waves surged, and floods flowed horizontally. Except for the mountainous areas, the entire territory of southeast Xuzhou and Haizhou became a swamp. The people's houses and livestock were washed away and drowned in large numbers. The half-ripe beans, sesame seeds, sweet potatoes, and other autumn crops in the fields were all submerged, with a flooded area of more than 300 square miles.

The Communist army in southern Shandong, intending to flood Haizhou City and Xinpu, also dug up the dikes of the Yi River in Linyi County, causing the river water to flow eastward and merge with the waters of the Shu and Yun rivers, overflowing into the Hai and Xin areas. The Wei River north of Xinpu was silted up for years, hindering drainage, resulting in water depths of several feet in the suburbs of Hai and Guan counties. The highway from Haizhou to Xinpu was cut off, and the Yangyu airfield was in danger of being submerged.

The local military and civilians in Xinpu were deeply concerned that the Yangyu airfield and streets would be flooded, so they joined forces on the 23rd and 24th to rush to build the Yanyan River embankment outside the Xinpu West Bridge and blocked several breaches in the airfield embankment. Under the scorching sun, the military and civilians worked hard, sweating like rain, showing no fatigue. Although the flood could not submerge Haizhou, the interruption of the food and fuel supply for hundreds of thousands of people in the Hai, Guan, and Lian areas is the most serious problem at present.

The Last Days of Japanese War Criminal Takashi Sakai

The poisonous net that Takashi Sakai spread in China killed countless Chinese soldiers, prisoners, and non-combatants. Now, this hatred deeply buried in the hearts of thousands of people has erupted with the execution of Takashi Sakai. (1) Lingering Athlete's Foot

Because the place was humid, in the summer of the following year, my feet (lower legs) felt rough. I fried and ate machine-milled rice bran, and took "Sanyou Industrial Society Athlete's Foot Medicine," which slightly reduced the swelling. In July of last year, the swelling of my legs returned as before. At that time, due to economic reasons, I used a folk remedy of eating several catties of boiled light red beans, but it was not effective. May I ask: (1) What is this exactly? What is the cause of the disease? (2) What is the impact of athlete's foot on the body? (3) Are there any effective medicines and preventive methods?

[Answer by Medical Doctor Yu Xinen] If it is athlete's foot, it will harm the heart. Injecting Vitamin B1: Injection medicine is very effective. In addition, a urine test should be done to see if there is kidney disease.

(2) Eye Pain

It does not cause redness or swelling when it occurs. He has to take painkillers one hour in advance to stop the pain. It recurred this summer as before, and painkillers are also ineffective. (1) If this continues, is there any danger to the eyes? (2) Is eating chives the cause of the disease? (3) Is this disease hereditary? (4) Is there any medicine that can cure it completely?

[Answer by Medical Doctor Yu Xinen] You should go to an ophthalmologist for examination and treatment, and do not randomly take medicine.

(3) Bladder Prolapse

It is painful when it is severe, but it returns to normal every morning after a good night's sleep. It recurs when I overwork. The pain is more severe after eating. It has been almost a year, and I don't know why. Because I live in a remote rural area, there is no good doctor to seek help from. Please give me a treatment method.

[Answer by Medical Doctor Yu Xinen] What you are suffering from is a small intestine hernia. Surgery is the radical cure. You can temporarily use a T-shaped belt to lift the scrotum, especially when working and walking.

Visiting the Father of the Three Suffering Sisters in Changshu, Gui Zhongfei 161

Living in Desperate Straits, Lonely and Helpless, It Is Truly Pitiable

Editor: My father, Gui Hong, alias Zhongfei, is 33 years old this year. He disappeared in the spring of the 30th year of the Republic [1941]. The reason is this: In January of the 26th year [1937], my mother died due to childbirth! In the autumn, because of the Japanese invasion, my father, grandmother, and I, along with my two younger sisters, fled to the countryside. Later, on a small boat, we lived a wandering life, having been to Gaoyou, Rugao, Nantong, Yancheng, and other places. I don't know when, perhaps in the autumn of the 29th year [1940], we arrived in the colorful Shanghai. This is heaven for the rich and hell for the poor. Three months after arriving in Shanghai, unfortunately, the three of us sisters all broke out with rashes. Beset by poverty and illness, and unable to find a job, my father spent every day borrowing money. Fortunately, our sisters' illness slightly improved. In order to reduce the burden on her beloved son, my grandmother returned to her hometown of Changshu, where the cost of living was relatively low. At that time, Changshu was still occupied by the Japanese. My father was afraid of being humiliated by the Japanese, so he stayed in Shanghai. At first, we still corresponded, but finally, one of my letters to my father was returned. I asked people to inquire, but it was in vain. Until now, it is still unknown whether he is alive or dead. Before I knew it, my father had been missing for a full five years! The three of us sisters lived a few years of childish life under the care of our grandmother, but heaven seemed particularly harsh to us. In the autumn of the year before last, it also took my grandmother away. The changes in our lives after my grandmother's death are beyond description. In short, our path to survival is almost over! I hope every day that my father can see the newspaper and return quickly to save his daughters from the depths of misery. At the same time, I also hope that kind people who know the whereabouts of my father will write to "Gui Mei, c/o Doctor Yi Mei, No. 47 Jiaotong Street, Changshu." I am a 16-year-old girl who just graduated from junior high school last year. Due to economic reasons, I did not continue my studies. My Chinese is not very good, so I would like to ask the editor to correct it and publish it as a favor. I respectfully wish you good health. Orphan Gui Mei, Fen and Rong together.

The Position and Attitude of a Daughter-in-Law 165

— Li Ying

Our country is a land of etiquette with a splendid history of five thousand years. Ethical concepts have always existed with dignity. Parents love their children, children respect their elders, husbands and wives are harmonious, brothers are respectful and fraternal. Every family is very harmonious. However, often many families, after marrying a daughter-in-law, have estrangement and jealousy, turning the harmonious atmosphere into one full of gloom and resentment, so that the entire family is not happy. Why is this?

Our ancestors lived under a large family system. Even now, the large family system has not been eradicated. In cities, only men and women with newer ideas have broken free from the shackles and established small families. "Large" and "small" are not changes in the system, but rather a shift in the perspective of 20th-century life. In large families, being a daughter-in-law is the most difficult and unrewarding job. She is surrounded by in-laws and sisters-in-law. If her husband has many siblings, she becomes the target of everyone, often the subject of their jokes, the object of cold ridicule. And what about her? She can only endure. She knows that this is an inevitable stage in life, and a natural result of the old system. Apart from gaining a little comfort in front of her husband, or placing all her hopes on her children, she can only get through it by silently accepting her arranged fate. She believes, "Years of being a daughter-in-law, years of being a mother-in-law, and then years of being a great-grandmother." She knows what it is like to be a daughter-in-law, and what it is like to be a mother-in-law. After tasting enough of the daughter-in-law's experience, she treats her daughter-in-law the same way. Instead of saying treatment, it is more like revenge. Generation after generation cycles through, until the increasingly innovative next generation can no longer endure this kind of "endurance," then there is strife and resistance. Those who can be independent break away and form small families, but most who continue to muddle along naturally have an even worse environment.

After organizing a small family, her position is invisibly raised. Now she is not a daughter-in-law but a wife, or even a mother. She is no longer restrained. A wife is equal to her husband. In addition to appropriate service and consideration, she does not need excessive service and submission, and no one deliberately bullies her or makes things difficult for her. Of course, this kind of life is not without small flaws, such as when economic difficulties are felt, when there are guests and she is too busy to manage, when there are too many children to care for, etc. Having family together can at least help her a little, but compared to the benefits, it is ultimately not a big deal.

Now it is time to talk about attitude. In large families that cannot be avoided, elders should use forgiving, loving, and optimistic eyes, holding the spirit of not being foolish, not being hypocritical, and not being an overbearing head of the family. Moreover, children and grandchildren have their own blessings, so there is no need to be jealous or curse. And those who are daughters-in-law should always remember that they are their elders, and should be filial and respectful, understand the psychological abnormalities that exist in the elderly. And being together every day, what's the point of tearing each other apart? With the attitude that both sides take a step back, they will definitely be able to live harmoniously, peacefully, and happily.

Although, to this day, we really don't need to maintain the large family system.

Three Prohibitions in Child Rearing 166

— Yunyu

The following are three important things about child rearing that I hope mothers will pay special attention to:

(1) Do not let people kiss your child. Many people often like to kiss children because they love them. This is a very common thing, and most mothers do not pay attention to it. In fact, we know that when kissing, the air exhaled by each other will be inhaled into each other. If the person kissing the child has a disease, it can be easily transmitted. If you want your child to stay healthy, quickly prohibit people from kissing your child!

(2) Do not deceive or scare your child. Children are curious. When they encounter something they have never seen before, they will ask, "What is this?" "Why is it like this?" Mothers should tell their children the reason why. If you don't know, answer frankly that you don't know. You must never deceive them with lies, or even threaten them. If the questions raised by children are often deceived or threatened, then the child's mind will be full of falsehood and fear, and their curiosity will also decrease or even disappear. Think about it: If people have no curiosity, how can all science and technology be improved day by day? I hope all mothers pay extra attention.

(3) Do not let people touch your child's genitals. Many people often like to touch boys' genitals, and most mothers think this is unimportant. If this continues day after day, it can easily cause the child to masturbate when they grow up. Everyone knows the drawbacks of masturbation, so there is no need to elaborate. At the same time, children must also be absolutely prohibited from touching their own genitals.

The Key to Beauty - Protecting the Skin 167

— Qing

Often some women, although they have very slender figures, because the foundation on their faces is applied too thickly, do not show any luster of the skin when they smile, completely like a colored plaster statue, unable to express any expression. At this time, if someone sees it at a glance, they will definitely feel very uncomfortable and feel a kind of pity for their skin.

We can be sure that a woman's appearance first focuses on the face, and the beauty or ugliness of the face depends on whether her skin is bright and smooth. Speaking of this, maybe someone will ask a question again, how can a woman's skin maintain its luster and radiance?

To maintain the beauty of the skin, we must first be able to protect the skin, so that it does not suffer damage from external stimulation. Anything that contains a large amount of lead, as well as too little sleep, are the most likely to irritate the skin. Therefore, women who usually like to apply relatively thick foundation that contains a lot of lead often have rough skin and enlarged pores. A woman who suffers from insomnia or stays up late often has rough and dry skin, and that's the reason. Therefore, the first important thing to nourish the skin is to carefully protect the skin.

Secondly, keeping the skin clean is also a way to nourish the skin, so within the possible range, it is best to avoid contact with dirty and dusty places, because unclean things contain a toxin that can absorb the skin's oil and make it dry. If this is not possible, then after you come back from walking, use clean warm water and soap to wash away the dust on your face, which is also a remedy; but after washing away the dust, the original oil on your face also fades away with the soap, so at this time we should use some nutrients to nourish it, such as egg white, glycerin, and the juice of fruits such as apples, oranges, and tomatoes, which are all good raw materials for nourishing the skin. (The above-mentioned ingredients are best used before going to bed, replacing soap to remove dirt. After getting up the next morning, wash with water, and the skin will appear radiant and smooth.) In addition, when the weather is cold in winter, you can apply lipid-based cosmetics (cold cream) to the face to prevent the skin from cracking.

If a woman's facial skin has reached the point of being clean and delicate, then apply a thin layer of foundation to her skin to cover up excessive oil on the face and remedy the sallow complexion, and then apply a small amount of rouge on this thin layer of powder, which can make the skin show a vivid and healthy beauty.

Re-making Old Pajamas into Casual Wear

Using Life to Teach Children 168

— Translated by Cheng Zhi

(1) The Branch Roads of Life

When I was young, I often argued with my younger brothers, even quarreled, because we were all stubborn and did things our own way.

One day, Father took us to the train station to play. We saw a train speeding towards us from both sides, and at the same time, a freight train was also rushing westward.

"What do you think will happen if two trains travel towards each other on the same track?" Father asked us.

We widened our eyes, thinking a terrible crash was about to happen, but as we watched, the freight train switched onto a branch road, letting the passenger train speed by safely.

"Look, children!" Father explained, "People are like trains, we are all moving in different directions on the same track. If there were no branch road facilities, there would be rifts between people, just like a train crash. Fortunately, we have many such facilities, such as patience, friendship, and tolerance. Therefore, between children, between adults, and even between countries, if they can always remember the branch roads in life, they will be more harmonious."

(2) Every Shot Counts

My father has allowed me to buy my first .22 caliber rifle. For many days, I have been flipping through the mail-order catalogs, and finally decided to choose a fully automatic one that fires fifteen rounds in succession. So I asked our bodyguard, Ping Jun, to agree to my choice, but he looked at the picture of the gun, then smiled and turned to me and said, "If I were you, I wouldn't want this one."

"Why?" I asked, suppressing my disappointment.

He said, "I think a single-shot is better. Every time you see this single-shot gun, you will think, if this shot doesn't hit, there will be no second chance. But, using an automatic is different, you no longer pay attention to the importance of each bullet, and as a result, you can't do the best you can."

Ping Jun's theory is indeed perfect. From then on, whether in career or in social life, I always think of his words, every shot counts.

(3) The Face and the Inside of the Watch

I remember one day when I was eleven years old, I returned home crying, because in the children's program at church, I was only assigned an insignificant backstage role. But my playmates were assigned the lead roles.

Mother quietly took out her watch and placed it in my hand.

"What do you see?" she asked me.

"The gold case face and the hands," I replied.

Then she opened the back of the watch and repeated the question. I now saw very small gears and screws.

"If any part is missing, even the ones you haven't seen yet, this watch is useless."

Her little lesson has made my life happier ever since, because I realize that everyone's work, even without others' admiration, is just as important.

Page 11

Spring and Autumn

Rossetti 169

— Pang Duoer

Dante Gabriel Rossetti was a poet and a painter. He dedicated his life to art, founded the Pre-Raphaelite Brotherhood, and led poets and artists of the late Victorian era, such as William Morris, Burne-Jones, and Swinburne, to engage in independent creation. His paintings are as famous as his poems. However, it is more accurate to say that there is painting in his poems, rather than poetry in his paintings. Because the main point of his paintings is color and atmosphere, not the narrative of actions.

Rossetti's artistic talent stemmed from his lineage. His father was an Italian writer who sought refuge in London because of his revolutionary ideas. His mother was born from the combination of an Italian and an Englishman. Therefore, all four of the Rossetti siblings possessed Italian artistic talents, and all achieved considerable success in art; however, Dante Gabriel, as the eldest, enjoyed the greatest fame.

Rossetti was born in London on May 12, 1828. At that time, his home was a gathering place for Italian fugitives. From a young age, he witnessed the activities of political figures, which instead made him develop a distaste for politics. He even lacked enthusiasm for Italy's independence movement. His love for Italy was solely for its literature and art.

Rossetti entered art school at the age of fourteen and the Antique School of the Royal Academy at eighteen. In addition to painting, he also loved Browning's poetry. At this time, he began to understand medieval culture and society, and translated many Italian medieval poems and Dante's *Vita Nuova*. Published, it became Rossetti's first work, and also the standard English translation of early Italian poetry.

In 1848, Rossetti formally founded the Pre-Raphaelite Brotherhood with his friends Holman Hunt and Millais, advocating the restoration of the pure and simple style of Italian painters before Raphael. This was a reaction against the craftsmanship that valued skill and adhered to conventions at the time. Their conclusion was: Raphael's painting skills were too perfect, making it impossible for later generations to develop their own paths, thus causing art to decline. Therefore, to reform art, it is necessary to transcend skills and express the soul, and first return to the artistic atmosphere before Raphael, and then create freely in order to achieve results. In their paintings, the themes, colors, structures, and various details are all different from those of their contemporaries, and they do not seek to please the mundane world. The most obvious point is that they disdain the superficial harmony of colors, and only use basic, strong colors. They also expressed this spirit in poetry. Their publication, *The Germ*, contained Rossetti's most famous poem, "The Blessed Damozel".

At this time, Rossetti met a young girl, Elizabeth Siddall. She had a slender figure, blue-gray eyes, full lips, and golden hair, which met the conditions of a medieval beauty, causing Rossetti, who loved ancient beauty, to become infatuated. He used her as a model, painting famous works such as Beatrice. Eventually, Rossetti married her. However, his temperament was so eccentric and his life so irregular that she felt extremely lonely and soon contracted lung disease. One night, when Rossetti returned home, he found his wife dead in bed. In grief, he buried all his manuscripts of poetry from recent years with her to show his repentance. Many years later, he listened to the advice of friends and exhumed the manuscripts from the grave.

In 1854, Rossetti met the famous critic Ruskin. Ruskin greatly supported him, establishing his position in the art world. Subsequently, Morris, Burne-Jones, and others were all influenced by Rossetti and abandoned their studies to paint. Later writers also admired and imitated him. However, after losing his wife, he gradually felt unwell physically and mentally. At that time, Buchanan and others attacked his poems, saying that they focused too much on describing the senses of the five organs and were overly immersed in sensual pleasures. Their ridicule made him feel very embarrassed, but he continued to write until he died of a stroke in 1882 at the age of fifty-four.

His poems are all written in a very casual style and contain the same idea, that is, men love women, symbolizing God's love for humanity, and the loveliness of women symbolizes the beauty of the soul. He believed that "life" is "love," and "life" and "love" are the same thing, because "love" is the driving force of the universe, and without "love" there is no "life." (Picture: Rossetti Self-Portrait)

Vivisection of the Heart 170

— Zhang Baihuai

"One evening, I saw you with your head lowered in dejection, wandering on the green field paths. Later, I saw you enlarging your throat and singing fervently. Are you making an expectation, or are you doing some necessary search?"

"No, I'm just following my own high notes."

"Then I would like to feel melancholic for your song. Just like the adorable morning sun facing the lonely building window. But did you notice us walking past you from behind at that time? And she whispered, your eyes must be fascinated by some difficult thoughts."

"Fascinated, yes, but why did you just walk past like that?"

"You were pondering at the time, saying that you were standing on the ruins of time and wanted to use the golden bricks of love to rebuild the desolation you saw. But you hesitated between yesterday and tomorrow, fearing that you would only pick up a prosperous dream. She almost couldn't help but laugh, but we finally didn't disturb you."

"I really don't understand why I fear the paleness of the soul, even the emptiness of thought. In these days, have you also seen me wandering in the loneliness of the depths of my heart?"

"Lonely people have no love, and you, the fire of love has burned your life red."

"Alas, although I say that I understand the meaning of life more than before, I have not yet turned to such a difficult-to-understand and chaotic chapter in the book of emotion. I ask all my friends, but until now, no one has been able to comprehend it. They all say that the wordless sentences are too vague, hidden and difficult. So, I have been doubting for a long time, doubting that it describes an unfortunate child who once used weakness and tears, angrily but powerlessly throwing pain into the forest of languid fate…"

"You are too indulgent towards yourself, but now it is a terrible demand."

"But a poet told me this, he said: When you are unable to continue forward, you stand by the road and see the pedestrians. I think this is the real cruelty."

"This time you have trusted yourself too easily."

"No, no, am I really so ignorant of myself? I walk on a narrow valley path, and what grows beside it is not lush flowers and trees, but thorns and bushes. Walking in the four directions, front and back, are not pedestrians and travelers, but wild beasts and leopards…"

"That's because you no longer have the will to continue climbing the road you dreamed of!"

"I really haven't thought about wavering and retreating, but my passionate heart is so lonely."

"Then have you heard a poet say? His sorrow is also his joy at the same time, perhaps your pain is also your sublimity at the same time."

"Yes, it's better to comfort myself like that. I remember I secretly thought, if someone really wanted to take themselves apart for dissection, and before they started, they declared that the life being dissected had already died, as a review of the final existence, perhaps no one would be willing to be cruel and give him a severe spiritual reproach…"

"But, is this your whole being?"

"Alas, you must be surprised by my poverty. What I think is profound and what I express is superficial, perhaps because I have lost too much and gained too little!"

"I don't want to spend too much time exploring the secrets of your heart. You can be proud of the dirty pearls on your forehead, and not be ashamed that you have not done better for more people. Go, if ridicule and jealousy continue, you will mercilessly throw a cold heart at them with the hatred of truth!"

Heine's Tragic Life 171

— Li Xia

Heinrich Heine was a romantic and passionate poet, but his life was one of suffering and misfortune. Between the duality of contradictions, he endured hardships all his life and could not turn over. Material and spiritual, ideal and reality, love and hate, passion and coldness, self-esteem and disappointment, these two-headed snakes of contradiction constantly attacked him.

"My heart, my heart's sorrow.

Although illuminated by the clear May sunshine,

I wander and lean under the linden tree,

Beside that high old city.

My chest is surging like the sea,

There are also hurricanes and tides,

Although it is said that there are beautiful pearls,

But it is a deep seabed."

……Homecoming Memories

The above little poem reflects the poet's inner sorrow. The poet was born in 1797 in the city of Dusseldorf on the Rhine. The city was originally German territory, but at that time it belonged to French rule, so in his "Memorandum" he said:

"I was born at the end of the suspicious eighteenth century, and my childhood was not only French, but also born in a city dominated by the French spirit."

And as Jewish parents raising him, it was exactly two extreme forces. The mother was a diligent and practical woman with a German style. Because she had the mentality of making her son an official, she ordered him to study law. However, the father was a cheerful, hedonistic, and optimistic person with a French style, and did not give any effective facilities to the education of his son. In such an atmosphere, the poet Heine began his contradictory life.

Relying on his mother's will, the poet moved to Hamburg at the age of nineteen to engage in the study of law. For a time, he dreamed of becoming a lawyer or a school professor in the future, and he also spent three months of first love. In particular, the result of this three-month first love had to embark on the tragic of the fate. In fact, the other party admired by the poet did not hold any such feelings. The scars of this painful experience first cast a black shadow on his poems. In the first half of his first collection of poems, "Book of Songs", the tone of painful sorrow for the past nightmare is permeated.

When he left this "cradle of distress," Hamburg, it was in the summer of 1819. Because he received the assistance of his uncle, he entered the University of Bonn to study law. In Bonn, he made many friends in the student union with a high degree of patriotism. He saw the student union disbanded, and he participated in the grand victory memorial festival of Carl Ludwig Sand, so the thought of resistance struggle gradually became extremely in his mind.

In the spring of 1821, he began to live in Berlin. In this prosperous metropolis, he was more deeply affected by both the bright and dark sides. But the problem that he felt particularly painful here was the concept of racial discrimination. As a Jew who was repeatedly subjected to embarrassing contempt, he expressed his anger and aversion in everything. Here, he gradually strengthened his anti-resistance atmosphere, and finally participated in the "Jewish Cultural Science Association", wrote articles, and even carried out his propaganda activities everywhere.

In 1825, he finally passed that annoying graduation exam and got a doctorate. And with the help of his uncle, he went to the North Sea again. The sea is what the poet especially likes. Due to the guidance of the sea, he finally crossed the sea to England. The sea gradually led him to the embrace of nature, promoting the wanderlust of this born wanderer. As a result of his roaming, he wrote masterpieces such as "The North Sea" and "Harz Journey", and published the work "Book of Songs" in 1827, which established his poet's reputation.

But the ideological and political opinions expressed in the collection of poems aroused opposition and attacks from backward forces everywhere. Even some parts were banned from sale by the Prussian government, and the pressure of disillusionment and misfortune gradually increased around him. So the poet arrived in Paris, France in May 1831.

The first impression in Paris was very strong and fresh. The nostalgia for Raf Antiero, Rousseau, Napoleon, and all other great French past was surging in his chest like a tide. It is even more interesting than everything else is the new religious theory of Saint-Simon. This theory enabled him to find a mediation between the democratic views he had always held and the emerging aristocratic artisticism. This theory advocates abolishing the old inequality, and replacing it is the expectation of a new class built by the ability of personality without following the tradition. At the same time, due to the love and cohabitation of Mathilde, a twenty-year-old girl, his passion burned even more, so that he could regard the suffering of the people as his own suffering, and take the people's social progress as his urgent vanguard.

"I am a sword, I am a flame. Please put a sword on my coffin. I am a brave warrior in the human war of freedom."

He was shouting like this, although he was rejected by the Parisians. However, he finally stood up as a savior of his motherland, and stood up as a supporter of the people.

But Heine was ultimately a "art for art's sake" poet. Because he was born with sensitivity, the degree of his love and hatred often had to go beyond the norm. So the poet's later poems replaced the happiness he had previously gained in poetry with ridicule and humor.

After 1842, he had a severe attack of chronic disease, which eroded and numbed the poet's hands, feet, and even eyelids. The later life of the hemiplegic poet became even more bleak. But precisely because of the disease, he had more time to fantasize, and finally wrote a narrative poem. After eight years of long suffering on the sickbed, he finally ended this "defeated" life on the morning of February 17, 1856.

The Tree and the Eagle 172

— Chen Ji

A young cypress tree, standing with its broad chest, stood in the boundless vast grassland, shaking its upper body and laughing freely all day long, singing heartily. All he saw was the happy blue sky and the happy white clouds.

One evening, the purple twilight shrouded the grassland, and the sun shed its haggard yellow hair. A piece of darkness swept over the branches of the pomelo tree, and the young singer felt melancholy. At this time, a large eagle flew over, flapped its wings and rested on the branches of the pomelo tree, with fresh red blood still dripping from its chest. It was dark, and the eagle cried sadly in the bleak night wind.

"Hey, is there anything in the world that hurts you?"

"In the world, oh friend, there are too many sorrows for wanderers in the world, and too many conspiracies for cruel people. They are jealous of me flying freely, and secretly, they aim their guns at me…"

"Don't people love freedom and happiness?"

"Oh friend, people want to kill freedom and happiness!…"

The next morning, the pomelo tree looked up to sing to the rising sun, but the sun did not come out, and the sky was full of gray clouds. The eagle fell from the tree like a stone, lying on its back at the foot of the pomelo tree. From then on, the eagle closed its bright eyes and no longer flew high, and the pomelo tree also lowered its head and became mute.

Again in the evening, a fat city merchant came and ordered two people to saw off the young pomelo tree. In its own panicked shouts, the pomelo tree broke its upper body and fell on the grassland. So the workers carried the tree and picked up the eagle and took them to the city to sell them. And the grassland was empty, losing its young singer!

Days went by, seasons changed, and rain and snow constantly washed over the grassland, leaving no wood chips from the tree or bloodstains from the eagle!

Wait for the roots of the pomelo tree to grow branches and stems again, and the era will be newly changed!

An Inch of Mountain, an Inch of River, an Inch of Blood 173

— Ye Jingfeng 35

This special agent leader in Beiping seemed quite shrewd, but unfortunately he encountered a troublesome problem at this time, and he was pacing around there, unable to handle it, and he was so distracted. His way of dealing with me was very similar to that of the "pig" deputy captain, offering as much high-quality tobacco, alcohol, and food as possible.

"Based on my humble opinion, your Excellency's tour is probably nothing more than the issue of the deputy captain of the Third Team of the 131st Liaison?" He wanted to get my tone with some tipsiness and cunning. He used the word "Your Excellency" because the identity I fabricated was equal to his.

Who is the deputy captain of the Third Team of the 131st Liaison? You probably still remember the "pig" who was killed by Little Tiger using grappling techniques to pull out his throat. The matter was only twenty-odd hours apart, and that scene was still active in my memory, of course. But I was surprised when he suddenly mentioned it to me.

"What's going on?" I pretended to be a little drunk and as if I knew it all along.

"This matter was allocated by the headquarters. Your Excellency came from the headquarters, don't you understand? …Perhaps you look down on me, because my position is very ordinary, so you are not willing to confide in me." He put on a close and very flattering look.

"The matter happened in your area. I started from Fengtian. The fastest trip would take one or two days. I'm afraid I wouldn't have received the news so quickly!" I was still vague, but I paid close attention to his expression.

"Although it is slow to come from Fengtian, can't you take a plane? Besides, with my humble eyes, I can determine that your Excellency must have come from Tianjin. The headquarters must have telegraphed your Excellency. This is still just a guess. In fact, the small intelligence of our area notified us of your Excellency's arrival early." He said, giving a fake laugh, but he was afraid of being too presumptuous, so the fake laugh stopped halfway and he apologized repeatedly.

"I have heard some rumors about the matter," I said, putting on a serious face, since he insisted that I was a commissioner sent by the headquarters to investigate the case: "I still need your Excellency to explain the whole case from beginning to end, so that I can decide what to do next, because the matter has been reported to the headquarters, it's always a bit troublesome, and it's also your Excellency's responsibility!" I took the opportunity to scare him and at the same time decided to take advantage of the opportunity.

"Regarding the case, I received an order from the marching headquarters of the 106th Division this morning, saying that Kiyono Shiro, a deputy captain of the Third Team of the 131st Liaison, and a driver from the same team, have disappeared at the same time." This guy was indeed scared, and immediately put away his smile. "I immediately ran to the Third Team's garrison to investigate in person. According to the clues reported by several people present in the Third Team, and together with a military intelligence officer from the 131st Liaison, we tracked down the missing vehicle. Then we found two bodies drowned in the water, which were the missing persons themselves."

"Isn't that murder?" I deliberately speculated to see if he wanted to muddle through the matter casually, or if he wanted to get to the bottom of it. "Are there any injuries—such as knife wounds or gunshot wounds?"

"It looks like a murder. The injuries…are…" He rolled his eyes and paused for a moment, "Because the bodies were swollen…"

"Murder must have a mastermind, so who is the mastermind?" I knew he hadn't paid attention to the injuries, so I was eager to know their relationship with me and Little Tiger.

"The difficulty lies in this point. It is said that the deputy captain was ordered to escort two senior officials sent by the headquarters to Beiping to handle important business; one of them is a special agent from Manchuria, a young man only twenty years old."

"Maybe these two are the masterminds?" I deliberately pressed forward.

"In fact, it is probably impossible, because the deputy captain made it very clear in front of his headquarters subordinates and soldiers; he said that they were two distinguished guests, one was a special commissioner from the headquarters, and also his classmate and old friend…"

"So, the bodies of these two distinguished guests…oh, haven't their traces been found?"

One of the most popular songs, "Silver Threads Among the Gold," was written by Hart P. Danks as a love song for his wife, but he sold the rights to the publisher for only fifteen dollars.
