Plain Tea 176

— Shao Fu

Since the investigative teams have gone to work in various places, there is hardly a place where problems have not been found. We hear about these endless corruption scandals every day, and besides feeling sad, we also feel suffocated. What conclusion will be drawn from this phenomenon is self-evident; it is extremely dangerous!

Some people regard the investigative teams as plain tea teams, as something light and bland, thinking they are merely helping to stir up conversation. Although the investigative teams in various places are working fairly and earnestly, such as Mr. Liu Wendao having the courage to catch tigers, and Mr. Qian Gonglai having the determination to receive tears, they really cannot investigate everything, and there are too many people involved. When the deadline arrives, they are handed over to ×× to continue handling and finishing the matter.

After careful study, the main obstacle to the investigative work in various places so far is "no original inventory list." Without the original inventory list, how can one investigate whether the takeover conforms to the records? However, as far as we know, every enemy-puppet organization, factory, or school at the time had an original inventory list, especially the Japanese. They knew about future compensation issues, and that these transferred materials would be used to offset the compensation, so they would never be sloppy in the slightest. As for the puppet organizations, they were naturally terrified and hoped to be pardoned for their efforts in safekeeping, so they made everything clear. In this situation, if there is no original inventory list, we dare to assert that there must be doubts. Therefore, the investigative team can sell what is turned over, but cannot lightly gloss over it with this reason.

It has been a full year, and we are still wallowing in taking over, handling, and investigating, in a chaotic and dizzying state, which is really disheartening.

Occasional Musings

Everyone Fears Death, Everyone Dies - Let's Talk About How to Live Long 177

— Yang Yongzhang

A mouse, even if it doesn't die in the claws of a cat, its lifespan is only three or four years. If you can prove that there is a mouse in the world that has indeed lived for ten years, you will immediately be surrounded by many scientists studying the problem of life. A ten-year-old mouse is undoubtedly considered long-lived; but if the dead person in the small coffin also happens to be ten years old, no one but a madman would say that he is long-lived. This suggests to us that longevity does not only refer to the length of years, because this has a great relationship with the species of the animal. The standards for humans and mice are certainly different, and even among humans, they are not the same. Leaving aside other things, it is said that the lifespan of the yellow race is relatively short. Japanese statistics show that only about 150 out of every thousand people can enjoy a lifespan of seventy years, but there are indeed many long-lived people in countries such as Bulgaria, Finland, and Norway. This has a considerable relationship with geographical conditions (such as climate and temperature); at the same time, they all pay attention to personal hygiene. Physical health preservation can certainly affect lifespan, and psychological changes, personal outlook on life, and lifestyle are all related to lifespan.

In addition to individual conditions, heredity is also important. "Like father, like son." There was a centenarian in Burgen who was 160 years old, and his son was already 103 years old. In a court in a certain place in the United States, in order to resolve a lawsuit, witnesses were summoned. He brought two sons with him, the older one was 102 years old, and the younger one was already 100 years old. His own age is self-evident. In a Vienna nursing home, doctors investigated 700 elderly people who were already eighty years old and learned that the parents of these elderly people were also mostly over seventy years old. Now I tell you that if your father can live to be ninety years old, you may (not necessarily) also be a centenarian in the future.

On the death certificates of patients, doctors write those terrible disease names, but medical scientists are eagerly hoping for the day when medicine can not only treat diseases, but also make further progress in preventing diseases, because diseases often destroy people's lives, making them unable to live long. Although doctors cannot create life, if people are not attacked by diseases, longevity can be obtained without effort.

Bacteriologist Metchmikoff believed that the bacteria in the human large intestine are the main cause of "short life." You may want to find a way to kill all the bacteria in the intestine to ensure longevity, but in fact this is fundamentally impossible. The bacteria in the large intestine are an indispensable medium for digestive function, and there is no way to remove the bacteria, but at least maintaining the health of the stomach and intestines can make people healthy. The reason why vegetarians live longer is because fermentation is less likely to occur in the intestines (meat is more likely than vegetables).

Nutrition can also affect longevity. Do you think a malnourished person will live long?

Some people argue that the weight of the brain is also related to lifespan, the heavier the longer, but this cannot be proven yet.

Longevity, longevity, people all hope for longevity, but in fact, I think too much longevity loses the tension and fun of life. Imagine if everyone could live to be a thousand years old, this world would probably be even worse.

I do not seek longevity, I only hope to strive to create my own fulfilling life in a short period of time.

Also Talking About Plagiarism 179

— Wen Zongkong

Literary plagiarism was discovered in ancient times, but it mostly belonged to poets. They occasionally extracted one or two good lines from the poems of their predecessors to make their own works more colorful. The purpose was to steal some fame, and there was no idea of profit. For example, He Xun's poem "Thin clouds emerge at the edge, the first moon crosses the middle." Du Fu changed four words, "Thin clouds rest at the strict edge, the lonely moon turns in the waves," and it became a Du Fu poem. Also, Lin Bu's poem "Bamboo shadows slant across the shallow clear water, osmanthus fragrance floats in the yellow dusk moon." Changed "bamboo" to "sparse" and "osmanthus" to "dark," and it became his plum blossom poem.

But today, the trend of plagiarism is flourishing, and there is a distinction between open and smuggled. The former is like the "Digest" publications published on the market. They have only two purposes: (1) Because readers cannot easily see all the good articles, they implement a wide search and selection, collecting and publishing them to facilitate readers' reading. (2) Because of this, their expenditure on manuscript fees can be saved.

Often, there are some degenerate writers who, under the threat of life, feel that it is difficult for their substandard articles to be accepted and published by editors in general newspapers and magazines, so they have to take risks and use despicable brains. They flip through better articles that have been published elsewhere several years ago, or some humorous translations from obscure magazines, change their appearance, copy them well, and send them to the newspaper office. Such manuscripts are naturally easy to publish, so they can wait quietly for the manuscript fee.

However, the editor who is in the position of a gardener, although he cherishes his own garden very much, it is difficult for him to meticulously identify the complicated seeds sent from various farms with his limited power and time. Therefore, it is not until the arrival of tourists that they will point out that this is an unworthy weed, and that is a flower that has mutated!

In the garden of Free Talk on the tenth of this month, a Mr. Huai Yizi also discovered during a visit that the article "Intelligence and Fool" published on August 1 under the name of "Ling Zhuoyan" was plagiarized from the article "Intelligent People and Fools" by Mr. Danxin on page 124 of the "Tide" series published on June 12, 1944. I think this person is very bold, but what is interesting is that the title of the exposed article happens to be "Intelligence and Fool". Is it that the God of Literature is playing tricks on the literary plagiarist in the dark, saying that he has turned from an intelligent person into a fool?

After reading the exposure of plagiarism published by the "Editorial Office," the plagiarist is miserable enough. Under such circumstances, it seems unkind to us to "not talk about their shortcomings" behind their backs, but considering this precious inch of land, in order to protect the growth of good crops and to take care of the gardener's energy, we, a group of visitors to the garden, have to grit our teeth, release our sharp eyes, and assist the editor to remove the tares that mix fish eyes with pearls, so that we can get a good harvest in the future!

Random Thoughts on Current Affairs

Who Pays the Bill? 180

— Fan Zhengbang

Mayor Wu said that buying the racecourse in two years will "take the wool from the sheep," which seems to mean buying the racecourse with the money collected from the racecourse, which is a great deal. In fact, who is the sheep that produces the wool? Isn't it the Chinese people? Isn't the wool that foreigners allow to be given to the city government taken from the Chinese sheep? At the same time, foreigners have taken away even more wool. This statement is accurate only if it comes from foreigners. Mayor Wu's calculation has been beaten by foreign merchants. We, the onlookers, are clear. This is the key to Mayor Wu's political reputation. If I were Mayor Wu's brain trust, I would advise Mayor Wu to follow the resolution of the Senate, which is the best policy. If we add persuasion, it is the worst policy. If we can oppose it, it is the best policy. If we say that we will buy it in two years, who can guarantee it? At the end of last year, 5,000 yuan of legal tender could buy a dan of good white rice, but now we cannot buy a dou of good rice. It is better to gather investment now or jointly operate beneficial businesses with Chinese and foreign parties on this huge base. I think it is better to refuse them outright than to take their money after they have run away and then prohibit them from running away?

Two points: First, who pays the bill? Second, who can guarantee what will happen in two years? Dear Mayor, respect the opinions of the people! The people will support you!

The Principal's Wishful Thinking 181

— Changpu

Yesterday, my friend Mr. Zhang came to visit. Because we are both in the education field, the topic was inseparable from our profession, and then we talked about the issue of teachers' advancement and retreat. He told me a scandalous thing that made me have to record it so that readers know that there is such a ridiculous thing in the world.

The thing is like this: On August 25, Mr. Zhang saw an advertisement in the newspaper that a certain elementary school in Pudong planned to hire several male and female teachers. He sent his resume. Two days later, he received a letter asking him to go to a certain elementary school on Daxi Road on the morning of the 29th for an interview and trial teaching. He thought that things must be slightly hopeful, but he did not know that when he went to the school that morning, it turned out to be a simple Weitang elementary school with only sixty or seventy students. The principal also served as the bell ringer, the school worker, the student who carried the organ, and the one who made boiled water, and also did chores. The principal was full of airs and showed an indifferent attitude, which made Mr. Zhang suspicious. Later, he was asked to teach several hours of classes that day, without water to drink, and he was exhausted and his mouth was dry before he was allowed to go back. He was told temporarily that whether he was hired or not, he would definitely receive a reply the next day, but Mr. Zhang waited five or six days after returning home, and there was no news at all. Knowing that he had been fooled, he had spent his own money and taught for him in the hot weather, "losing his wife and losing his army." It turned out that the shrewd principal was afraid that the students would not be able to stay if school started late, so he started classes early; but he did not want the old teachers to be paid from August, so he came up with this method. To put it nicely, it was asking new teachers to try out teaching, but in fact, it was saving himself the expense of salaries for August.

All of this is truly speechless.

News Figures

Liu Wendao, Head of the Fujian-Taiwan Investigative Team, Goes to Taiwan to Fight Tigers 182

— Jun Mo

Liu Wendao, head of the Fujian-Taiwan Takeover Work Investigative Team, arrived in Taiwan and hosted reporters on the 12th, saying, "We have come to Taiwan this time to fight tigers, not to swat flies."

People who have met Liu Wendao can believe that he can fight a few tigers: tall stature, strong build, square head and big ears, although he always seems to have a smiling face, he doesn't talk much, making it difficult to guess what he wants to do.

Military Background

This is a politician with a military background. Half of his life's work has been spent in his hometown of Hubei, and Liu Wendao has a particularly long relationship with Hankou; the other half has been spent abroad—Germany and Italy. After graduating from Baoding Military Academy, he, like many of his classmates, went to Japan, but he always seemed to have little interest in leading troops, so he soon went to France to study law at the University of Paris. When he returned to China, it was just as the Northern Expedition was unfolding; he, a young man in his thirties who had studied military affairs and then turned to the path of law, served as the director of the political department of the Forward Headquarters of the National Revolutionary Army. After the Northern Expeditionary Army occupied Hankou, he took office as the mayor of this city, which is the hub of north and south. At that time, Hankou, which had been occupied by warlords for a long time, was still in a mess, especially because Hankou had special zones and French and Japanese concessions, which made governance even more difficult. Taking transportation as an example, the rickshaws in Hankou could not be pulled into the special zones and concessions, and the rickshaws in the special zones and concessions could not be pulled out. This matter caused a lot of difficulties in transportation. After Liu's many negotiations with the concession authorities, the "military passage" between the two sides was finally successful. But unexpectedly, this small "international negotiation" was precisely the beginning of his long diplomatic career.

Once Envoy to Germany

In the 20th year of the Republic, Liu served as the minister to Germany; later, he was transferred to the minister to Italy. In the years before the war, the relationship between China and Italy was quite good, especially in aviation. There was a lot of cooperation in aircraft and flight training. At that time, most of the foreign instructors at the Central Aviation School at Jianqiao in Hangzhou were Italians. Liu made great contributions to the work in aviation cooperation. However, in the 26th year, when the August 13th Incident broke out, these ungrateful Italian instructors sat in Japanese bombers and bombed the Hangzhou fire station into an empty shell, which Liu could not have foreseen at the beginning!

Quite Humorous

Liu Wendao is quite humorous, but he is not willing to be lenient. When he was the mayor of Hankou, there was a very famous geomancer named Ding Shouyang who had been in Hankou for more than 20 years. He specialized in looking at the feng shui of tombs, and it was said that he was always accurate. A director in the city government admired him so much that he introduced him to the mayor's residence to find a good burial place for the ancestral tomb. This feng shui master boasted in front of Liu Wendao that after looking at this tomb, he would definitely be rich and prosperous for generations to come. Liu remained silent. After he finished speaking, after a long time, he slowly asked, "Since that's the case, why don't you find one for yourself first?" He drove the geomancer, who had been poured a bucket of cold water, out of the gate.

This was naturally just swatting a fly, but Liu is now going to see the feng shui of Taiwan for himself, and he will probably be able to pull a similar cold face and beat a few tigers back!
